# Changelog

## 0.169.0

- Extended the dependency-free Claude saved-workflow compiler with bounded `+` text composition for direct, pipeline, and static-parallel prompts plus labels. Text operands remain inert syntax; numeric arithmetic, calls, mutation, helpers, and general expressions remain rejected rather than evaluated.
- Preserved static `meta.whenToUse` discovery guidance through loading and inspection, and added static per-agent `effort` for direct and mapped calls. Shared `low`/`medium`/`high`/`xhigh` values pass through, while Claude `max` maps to Codex `ultra`; dynamic effort, model, custom-agent, and worktree options remain explicit gaps.
- Added `validate-saved-workflows --keep-going` for complete non-executing corpus diagnostics, effort visibility in workflow inspection, adversarial compiler/CLI coverage, and a real packaged parallel fixture that proves concatenation, discovery metadata, and the `ultra` execution binding without a provider call.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.169.0`. All 1,032 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 3 saved scripts, 92 release-owned strict JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, four byte-identical builds, and seven final 185/185 matrices pass. The guarded installer immediately returns `already-installed` without approval on an identical rerun, the Codex companion host is healthy, and real Codex marketplace ingestion reports plugin `0.169.0` enabled with cached runtime bytes matching the release artifact. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `c433b27ee3b998c83d7342965c0b95f0164aba80174ca16cfcd1639eef03a0e9`, `19ac59bde0c31bee9d2d1f534319fcf17c4ac1e190593f253e4ffcef99a35c26`, `6b2b0ed0dfaf71646d61084e6d3e4fbae5f1dc895846a427aa679bfbb213e05d`, `5732502998a39d0d3e1126de54ac25aa8268579ea94eedecb87cf354be92540e`, `1e8582abc5b5ec9b43ae158cf8de04c0b2350bdf15384ea0cf2719d1b63f7f9f`, and `cd8c896352b034eddf1a09f9831abe8578642d576fa3873886c3ece07e7ba4a1`. No model/provider, paid Codex, or Claude call was used to implement, package, install, or verify this release.

## 0.168.0

- Added dependency-free static compilation for common Claude `phase()` and `parallel(SOURCE.map(item => () => agent(...)))` workflows. JSON-compatible constants, static object-property prompt interpolation, schema constants, declared phase metadata/options, dynamic argument sources, and terminal `.filter(Boolean)` now compile into the existing audited runtime without evaluating JavaScript.
- Added `agent_map.item_semantics: "opaque"` for bounded inline prompt text. Workspace-path semantics remain the default; opaque sources use hash-and-size identity and never resolve prompt text through the workspace filesystem, while cache, terminal recovery, retry, and drift checks retain deterministic binding.
- Added adversarial compiler/runtime/schema coverage, a real parallel/phase benchmark fixture, packaged `.pyz` dry-run coverage, compact inspect visibility for workers/phases/opaque items, and two provider-free parity-matrix checks. Arbitrary JavaScript, helper functions/control flow, nested fan-out, promise/arbitrary transforms, richer pipeline callbacks, and write-capable script compilation remain explicit gaps.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.168.0`. All 1,028 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 3 saved scripts, 92 release-owned strict JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, eight official Skill validations, four byte-identical builds, and six final 184/184 matrices pass. The guarded installer immediately returns `already-installed` without approval on an identical rerun, the Codex companion host is healthy, and real Codex marketplace ingestion reports plugin `0.168.0` enabled with cached runtime bytes matching the release artifact. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `4eb8a2f0085b3198d56fdb5d49456cc79a88c6b4db5d903af85eaec0b2f8d2ef`, `0dac278d080174b430a6a2230174afcce87ae718f4c9d0e0b760182ff3a36df5`, `3dfe86b39a2ee8373beba304299dd03fe0d2b5bf3460aacd7d8e924771bdc0fc`, `ca65474cc105c4042409a62ca539a89759057eb1e06a42c5c10eb913124c16f9`, `51508a57e8e200c077dce4bc2851c42522539bb73f4a65a338379fb24a2f87f2`, and `11990450aee6069be7d37b18d4269d2506425903cab59095201d227e4c38b8bc`. No model/provider, paid Codex, or Claude call was used to implement, package, install, or verify this release. The complete external release evidence is hash-manifested and recursively read-only.

## 0.167.0

- Added an optional terminal workflow result contract: one declared `result_artifact` is owned by exactly one final `collect_results` step over a completed direct or map dependency. Collection is local and zero-provider, preserves ordered map multiplicity, emits bounded canonical JSON, and applies JavaScript-compatible falsey filtering only when explicitly compiled from `.filter(Boolean)`.
- Hardened collection and recovery with no-follow per-source reads, strict duplicate-free finite JSON, incremental aggregate bounds, ordered byte-level source receipts, output hashes and sizes, and resume-time source/result recomputation. Source drift, output drift, stale receipts, skipped dependencies, unsafe paths, and malformed or oversized values fail closed without provider replay.
- Extended the static Claude saved-workflow compiler to return `claude-workflow/result.json`, and added `--print-result` to fixed and saved workflow execution. Default output remains the result path only, avoiding automatic context expansion; dry-runs report the planned path and reject explicit rendering.
- Added adversarial compiler, validator, runner, CLI, resume, schema, and packaged `.pyz` coverage, plus provider-free parity-matrix checks for the public contract and explicit result interface. General JavaScript control flow, `parallel()`/`phase()`, write-capable script compilation, and provider-native result UI remain explicit gaps.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.167.0`. All 1,022 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 92 release-owned strict JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, eight official Skill validations, four byte-identical builds, and six final 182/182 matrices pass. The guarded installer immediately returns `already-installed` without approval on an identical rerun, the Codex companion host is healthy, and real Codex marketplace ingestion reports plugin `0.167.0` enabled with cached runtime bytes matching the release artifact. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `9eb0624b7ef6db628116152dbfadb56a13eafc2369fddeab2f94eb143aee5cae`, `7b8f79d942d8f31997ee70e3d72c92efb723ef47f0fae04179c24e0e2c04d29b`, `1910e0db42b5a1cf014167a7d7c6d3a5c85d2688fbf378d45335dd3a28aebff8`, `102650b9646ea2ecd545c52b00e16e41ea98458a458f598fed7b66c1aecb676f`, `30e572e13410cf00603f132dd2e8bc4449739a2eba796b9c862f1e0342485fd1`, and `9f623bbe6e16b4cc4b5080da13d8922c52b24053f40123989a6aeba815de94b7`. No model/provider, paid Codex, or Claude call was used to implement, package, install, or verify this release. The complete external release evidence is hash-manifested and recursively read-only.

## 0.166.0

- Added a dependency-free static compiler for the documented Claude saved-workflow shape. Existing JSON-compatible `meta`/`workflow` exports remain unchanged; scripts without a workflow export may use bounded static literals, top-level awaited `agent()`/`pipeline()` bindings, structured `args`, prior-agent array-schema handoff, callback templates, and direct or `.filter(Boolean)` return. Compiled calls are read-only, preserve statement order, schedule one packet per item, and share Claude's 16-concurrent and 1,000-total ceilings.
- Added optional inline `output_schema` for `codex_exec` and `agent_map`, materialized as a private exact run artifact and passed through Codex `--output-schema`. `agent_map.items_pointer` now resolves strict duplicate-free JSON artifacts through bounded RFC 6901 pointers before applying all existing item path, secret, size, uniqueness, and count checks. Omitted fields preserve the prior command and line-oriented handoff.
- Kept JavaScript inert. The compiler has no Node dependency or evaluator and rejects imports, loops, branches, mutation, arbitrary calls, computed expressions, dynamic interpolation, unsupported options, forward references, schema mismatches, and trailing bodies with source-position diagnostics. Focused tests cover the exact official example, CLI validation/inspection/dry-run, declarative compatibility, structured args, schema normalization, JSON handoff, total-agent allocation, and adversarial rejection.
- Completed one preregistered exact-0.165 quota-ledger pair before implementation. Codex `gpt-5.6-sol` auto resolved to medium, scored 10/10, passed all 5 visible and 8 held-out tests, and delivered in 52.106 seconds with 26,178 gross tokens. Command-pinned Sonnet Ultracode used `claude-sonnet-5` with one Haiku helper and no Opus, spent `$0.20365`, 61.239 seconds, and 38,825 gross tokens before its budget failure without an edit or verification. This targeted row does not establish broad, universal, or cost superiority; authoritative Codex dollar telemetry remains unavailable.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.166.0`. All 1,013 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 92 release-owned strict JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, eight official Skill validations, four byte-identical builds, and six final 180/180 matrices pass. The guarded installer immediately returns `already-installed` without approval on an identical rerun, the previously missing Codex companion host resolves healthy, and real Codex marketplace ingestion reports plugin `0.166.0` enabled with cached runtime bytes matching the release artifact. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `0f08744ac027936aab8571c874192abd9cef1b95600d00100ba4933acab13c3a`, `d363158729408493b9f57670d757367a53df448eaa2b9b13ff2da7ab37ab98c9`, `3cb79b5051e1d4f26fd1ff5f6af56526cd5c6a098269fd8f0b5bf2f18e4053c2`, `35e0e8dbf1b98f87bf4643fbd2fa3eaf55bd5897eb73af82e1ada6e3b62f41bf`, `d0a21a27283d12a05c3537f5e074a04db6460d5aff2783c831987636f820762d`, and `3e4f6ab00f915a2eda4e2018a5ab2a4e81173c8c89f448253b26ed65b9436ad0`. No model/provider, paid Codex, or Claude call was used to implement, package, install, or verify `0.166.0`; the separately disclosed exact-0.165 matched pair was completed before implementation. The complete external release evidence is hash-manifested and recursively read-only.

## 0.165.0

- Added explicit one-command verified delivery to `run-claude-staged-task`, `run-codex-staged-task`, and `run-codex-staged-repair`. `--apply-verified-stage` preflights its fresh external receipt and `verified-stage-apply` approval before provider launch, writes strict evidence first, and then reuses the release-0.164 transaction with zero additional provider or verifier calls.
- Preserved non-applying defaults and every strict provider/report/repair artifact. An omitted exit contract remains strict normally and resolves to verified-stage delivery semantics only for the explicit inline apply path; an explicitly selected `strict` contract remains strict even after a successful transaction.
- Kept deletion authority independent through `--allow-destructive --approve verified-stage-delete`. Apply or deletion gate failures retain the verified stage for standalone zero-replay recovery, evidence-write failure prevents source mutation, and a pre-existing receipt fails before provider launch with a recovery instruction.
- Added adversarial Codex cutoff, report-write failure, receipt/approval preflight, deletion recovery, cumulative-repair, Sonnet-only Claude, no-replay call-count, and conservative shell-capability coverage without changing schemas, default provider calls, prompts, caps, dependencies, daemons, or repository-local state.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.165.0`. All 997 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 91 release-owned strict JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, three byte-identical builds, and six final 177/177 matrices pass. The guarded installer immediately returns `already-installed` without approval on an identical rerun, the Codex companion host reports healthy, and real Codex marketplace ingestion reports plugin `0.165.0` enabled with cached runtime bytes matching the release artifact. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `4d9bdfbd209cee21966c4a998639286cb7984ca11f3e7e364441644398bca167`, `8490f061a84367c77b895b45c9aacff99d19367412cd463297ad9ca576744e5d`, `f6c44809798eea9594a4160228ac8f7db7a3a0a9d28ede263b51866c09b69eb8`, `479e563e3670e46e4a8c9bf0f1b508eecf8dbd32a3dbfdf9c1888199d86984e4`, `d0a21a27283d12a05c3537f5e074a04db6460d5aff2783c831987636f820762d`, and `3e4f6ab00f915a2eda4e2018a5ab2a4e81173c8c89f448253b26ed65b9436ad0`. ## 0.164.0

- Added `apply-verified-stage`, a separate explicit zero-model transaction that converts an accepted one-result staged report or cumulative `repair.json` into source edits only after exact evidence, source, stage, path, change-set, and patch revalidation. Existing staged commands remain non-applying and all strict provider/report/repair outcomes remain unchanged.
- Added strict external `conductor.staged_apply.v1` receipts and `validate-staged-apply`. A single-link no-follow lock and durable `prepared -> merging -> merged` journal support recovery before source writes, during a partial ordered merge, and after all files landed; recovery accepts only exact before/verified values and never replays a provider or verifier.
- Split application authority from deletion authority. Every first apply requires `--allow-writes --approve verified-stage-apply`; any retained deletion independently requires `--allow-destructive --approve verified-stage-delete`. Approval values are absent from receipts, actual application is local/non-networked, and terminal fingerprint rechecks are approval-free and byte-identical.
- Added provider-free coverage for single-stage and cumulative-repair cutoff delivery, add/modify/delete behavior, original Git metadata preservation, source/stage/patch/evidence/path/receipt tampering, duplicate JSON, symlinks, prepared and partial-merge recovery, terminal idempotence, schema/CLI/security contracts, and zero provider/verifier replay. The packaged matrix now exposes both the public receipt schema and exact command help.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.164.0`. All 991 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 91 release-owned strict JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, three byte-identical builds, and six final 174/174 matrices pass. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `e5987af0d486e253c4bb6e1baf8cc9de6f6d03e8bd340b4b4b0e0eec203c434b`, `a0ae4e2736962785475c17f5d340ce73311309f08cf756dfd9a317e0693bfee3`, `ebd7a312b5eb3b03084dbc2461cef2548ebbb3a555bdcc59e98115d87c38d3a2`, `d233c9caeeea0b3d23ab905369363b0d66b50ba8d88bc2ec4a2b89b3a653e54c`, `35a2712ab200ecb5c7336e216a0edc604de60cdcb60375d431c2b0ef35df618c`, and `09961bf8a978c8391e1a5e553fc1bf4e0936e6815af876d8edd56dc2341cf8bb`. No model/provider, paid Codex, or Claude call was used to implement, package, install, or verify this release. Its complete external release evidence is hash-manifested and recursively read-only.

## 0.163.0

- Extended the strict-by-default `--exit-contract strict|verified-stage` interface to `run-codex-staged-repair`. A clean Codex token cutoff may now return process exit zero when the completed repair already retained a verifier-passing cumulative patch; repair status, provider failure, aggregate report, incidents, usage, comparisons, and source state remain unchanged.
- Added zero-call completed-checkpoint recovery: rerunning the same repair arguments with `--resume --exit-contract verified-stage` revalidates the completed state and can expose its retained delivery without replaying Codex or the verifier. Paused and uncertain active-attempt checkpoints remain nonzero and retain their existing recovery rules.
- The repair acceptance gate reloads strict repair evidence, revalidates its hash-linked final attempt report, applies the single-stage verifier/completion contract to the exact attempt patch, and independently reopens the cumulative `final.patch` with no-follow, exact-byte, and SHA-256 checks. Source drift, automatic apply, verifier mutation/failure, unsupported changes, malformed evidence, and patch/report races fail closed.
- Corrected capability documentation to reflect release `0.157.0` support for separately approved sandboxed Skill-local stdio MCP scripts. Arbitrary ambient or package-runner stdio commands remain unsupported.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.163.0`. All 983 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 91 strict source JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, three byte-identical builds, and six final 172/172 matrices pass. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `19cda46fe85d939e3114e2be2f0dc4a7c742e114b1f5b41e9a18ec29ca514966`, `d08dd4e625c8a5b65a57880a13dcb3731c20fc114b06bc605ce1b0a9bb26784e`, `bfe74d0ef5ca667d85611b523872917ab0d1742658911613932e62ea48e0cc25`, `581e04d4f536ffb38e1afb9dff5a73669595bcc555808f066b153c94b4045b05`, `39b9be19e80ce18a7f2465061f2fd960edfb2d56ff174794617a3d8114ba7d6d`, and `558ac08b1884afcce30444f3eaa9d04289d931e01da4b0c38424c71ac917b1b0`. No model/provider, paid Codex, or Claude call was used to implement, package, install, or verify this release.

## 0.162.0

- Added explicit `--exit-contract strict|verified-stage` to both staged provider CLIs. `strict` remains the default. `verified-stage` returns process exit zero only when existing validated evidence proves a non-empty retained patch, unchanged source, no verifier mutation, a configured passing isolated verifier, an agreeing completion summary, and no automatic apply. Provider status, benchmark/report failure, incidents, token/cost evidence, patch bytes, and comparison semantics remain unchanged.
- Corrected command-policy classification for the exact `--help` and `-h` shape of provider and campaign run subcommands. Help inspection is read-only; adding any other argument retains the command's ordinary write/network classification, so the packaged smoke matrix can inspect this interface without receiving write capability.
- Kept the 8,000-token low-effort ceiling instead of spending more merely to obtain provider final prose. The new exit contract adds no provider call, retry, cap, prompt, permission, dependency, or source mutation; no-change, failed-verifier, timeout, drift, malformed, patchless, and unsupported outcomes remain nonzero. `auto` retains its existing command-verifier acceptance path, while standalone shell automation can now choose the same outcome-first behavior explicitly.
- Sealed two exact-0.161 diagnostic campaigns outside the repository. In the two-task Codex effort campaign, low/8k delivered a 10/10 slug patch after a truthful provider cutoff and medium/16k completed a 10/10 migration at 13,315 exact weighted tokens; its 28-entry manifest SHA-256 is `4380f0ae0d71dde9cad01d1ba52ff500c32e376146d78d78f57da407be536d91`. In one preregistered matched migration pair, `gpt-5.6-sol` medium scored 10/10 and delivered in 39.766 seconds, while command-pinned `claude-sonnet-5` Ultracode used no Opus, exceeded its `$0.10` request at `$0.1165946`, produced no patch, and scored 0/10 in 46.497 seconds. That 12-entry manifest SHA-256 is `9144d64017baaab80a925bdc18b68c716f8eae78df92460d3731dd0df8727e40`. One stochastic pair is task-local evidence, not broad or universal superiority.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.162.0`. All 982 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 91 strict source JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, three byte-identical builds, and six final 171/171 matrices pass. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `bcbaf742fa252116ac9b244f3b630b55f319cbbc9b1d3cb4c3b7df1343ecee3c`, `d5ff2c0bae86a621b5580eac3a30208f6fd0f055860b8a3075c64fcd9f2eba3b`, `3e7ba28d5ac8507edec9cd880273cf575a096deefadf01cfe02b6485fdefc8a0`, `1e62b643f64ad2d4205c45b3cb2b9feb75e63a591d4be365c08398e3e8b8e820`, `39b9be19e80ce18a7f2465061f2fd960edfb2d56ff174794617a3d8114ba7d6d`, and `558ac08b1884afcce30444f3eaa9d04289d931e01da4b0c38424c71ac917b1b0`. No additional model/provider or paid call was used to implement, package, install, or verify this release.
- The verified read-only 522-entry release-evidence manifest is sealed outside the repository at SHA-256 `21f527bf18406160a09e32790b9922e284d7fc61974b7727d5e94aee28a5eb1f`.

## 0.161.0

- Added strict `conductor.codex_provider_evidence.v5` token-usage provenance and bounds. Exact completion usage remains exact; a future Codex `turn.failed` event carrying `usage` is retained exactly. When Codex 0.144.1 omits usage on a runtime-budget failure, v5 records gross and weighted usage as at least the requested hard cap with null upper bounds. It never fabricates an exact count or finite ceiling.
- Kept the hardened `codex exec --ephemeral --ignore-user-config --ignore-rules` adapter. The implementation does not switch to app-server, inspect persisted Codex sessions, copy credentials, retry the provider, or add a dependency. Strict v1-v4 provider evidence remains readable, and a new immutable v4 template preserves the prior contract.
- Added focused forward-compatibility, lower-bound, tamper, legacy-schema, generated-schema, dashboard, staged-repair, and provider-free matrix coverage. No paid Codex or Claude call was used for this implementation.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.161.0`. All 980 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 91 strict source JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, three byte-identical builds, and six final 170/170 matrices pass. ## 0.160.0

- Replaced the fixed 24,000-token omitted cap for deterministic direct writes with an effort-proportional table: 8,000/16,000/24,000/32,000/40,000 for `low`/`medium`/`high`/`xhigh`/`ultra`. `high` remains unchanged; low and medium stop inheriting high-effort funding, while xhigh and ultra receive the additional headroom their explicit effort requests imply. Read-only direct, planner, native, generated graph, map/team, and explicit caller caps are unchanged.
- Preregistered and ran one exact 0.159 `gpt-5.6-sol` low canary at an 8,000-token hard cap with no retry. It exhausted the cap and emitted no final message, but produced a source-isolated verifier-passing patch that scored 10/10 and killed all five hidden mutants, matching the sealed 12k run at a 33.3% lower ceiling. This supports the low-effort allocation for that frozen task, not a universal 8k sufficiency or causal latency claim.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.160.0`. All 980 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 90 strict source JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, two byte-identical builds, and six final 169/169 matrices pass. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `6846f9e750c3040ceebdc227bec4a530fef984e65f7a862d0c02c1bdbd9e81ec`, `5b16aafcbbef75dac52033f647058ded462e52a2f980ba7c0e771eacb30f6805`, `d1c7650639f193b4d570316c9f4e7da2b7250f9b342aa90a1309f072c95f46bb`, `2757acff61e2f678659a8dabca6a3c3c0649536810c694ba5180f8843d445aac`, `e1ced500d01ae1db3c13e823c3e85a0ca1078a81fb3790346ff31d773cf242a4`, and `5ff54ceb1ab80b67e12df7ab5519c9276f4853660f70622e8bc2ffefdbad6cd1`. The preregistered canary used one Codex provider call; no Claude call, retry, or provider call was used for implementation, packaging, installation, or release verification.
- The verified read-only 642-entry release-evidence manifest is sealed outside the repository at SHA-256 `1b1649334843fad297f2e11f8de9f399945b35604d459697f766ba429c406837`.

## 0.159.0

- Replaced the staged comparison wrappers with a lean provider-neutral prompt contract. On the exact frozen `backoff-test-authoring` task and source, the Codex prompt is 6,172 bytes instead of 8,219, saving 2,047 bytes (24.9%); Claude is 5,008 instead of 6,295, saving 1,287 bytes (20.4%). Codex's new prompt is also 123 bytes smaller than Claude's old prompt. These are exact deterministic byte measurements, not token, cache, latency, quality, cost, or superiority evidence.
- Removed repeated complete-context/no-discovery prose, collapsed the pointer-only test-authoring static-audit block into the one trusted task policy, shortened checkpoint/finalization wording, and changed the internal provider projection to `conductor.small_workspace_context.v2`. V2 retains sorted path/content/executable records but omits model-irrelevant workspace/per-file hashes, counts, and raw-size metadata; the parent still performs the same complete hash-bearing pre/post snapshot checks, content screens, and prompt-hash binding.
- Preserved the complete rendered task contract, generic public-contract checklist, metadata-only policy selection, representative behavior/fault coverage, baseline static tracing, import bounds including `Decimal`/`Fraction`, sandbox and verifier rules, Codex 90% first-write and 50% completion checkpoints, repair semantics, zero-tool finalization, source isolation, and no-automatic-apply behavior. The change adds no model call, retry, effort increase, token-cap increase, permission, network access, dependency, or repository state.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.159.0`. All 980 warning-strict tests, repository-wide Ruff, 19 workflows, 90 strict source JSON files, local/Skill/archive/install/marketplace/doctor/state audits, two byte-identical builds, and six 169/169 matrices pass. ## 0.157.0

- Added backward-compatible selected-Skill stdio MCP routes to restricted profiles. A strict `transport: "stdio"` dependency names one already-selected Skill, one executable non-empty resource under `scripts/`, exact arguments, and exact tool names. Codex's own bounded `skills/list` metadata must contain one matching `type: mcp`, `transport: stdio`, expansion-free command. Every route requires `skill-mcp:<name>` plus separate `skill-mcp-stdio:<name>` approval; unlike HTTPS routes it grants no runtime network capability and accepts no auth, environment, URL, interpreter, package runner, or arbitrary executable.
- Added a dependency-free ephemeral stdio proxy. Every actual direct, map, team, or guarded same-thread provider call revalidates the complete Skill binding, copies it into a fresh external immutable snapshot, strips sibling execute bits, gives the child only a sanitized fixed environment and private writable temp, and passes Codex only a receipt/hash-bound Conductor self-command. The proxy rehashes every file/mode before launch and supervises one recorded process group. macOS Seatbelt denies workspace/home access, network, forking, and non-runtime writes; Linux bubblewrap uses network/PID namespaces, hidden home/root, read-only runtime roots and snapshot, and one private writable bind. Receipt/snapshot drift, unsupported hosts, and missing sandbox tools fail before the selected program runs.
- Preserved ordinary Codex continuity and the zero-route fast path. Stdio routes get a fresh snapshot/proxy on direct execution, each parallel map packet, team calls, and `recover-run --resume-codex`; HTTPS auth can compose with the same command rewrite. Profiles without stdio retain their prior command shape. Transport counts now appear in profile inspection, state, packet traces, team aggregates, and dashboards without temporary paths or contents. No daemon, persistent MCP server/config, ambient credential, transcript, repository `.codex`/`.codex-conductor`, or other repository runtime state is added.
- Provider-free verification covers strict schema/command/resource matching, transport-specific approvals, inert pre-launch config, source and packaged proxy dispatch, immutable snapshot identity, tamper rejection, real macOS filesystem/network/environment isolation, cleanup, direct/map/team route freshness, and actual same-UUID checkpoint recovery. Selected program behavior and MCP output remain untrusted semantic input; this release does not support arbitrary ambient/package-runner stdio dependencies or claim live Linux execution evidence.
- Shipped and actively installed exact `0.157.0`. Runtime, bundle, marketplace, release-manifest, Skill-archive, and Skill-tree SHA-256 values are `d6777c621c41154542a3f70073a18a9a7ed6f2e89781050a259d3755f12cf780`, `be6f590894621408b2fefb675b854c5ce2add6204020c4d88a4e47a3ec527071`, `b5ee78329786b1272d71ca6de5ae7462a94e7a9f64a96e63f8282986c94234f0`, `f926b8daeb4b6facc80e5beb92344f327902dc1401cb2135b0e78615b1431f07`, `39e3a4839b74959b0f6dd4cc15c9168e8ae826398067363af301c92dd87cbe1e`, and `e5e7b825ff59c5666d18a553e4cd7df64d0f4b858be00d831b59d170c9c06c76`. ## 0.156.0

- Replaced temporary authenticated Codex homes with a dependency-free in-process loopback broker created for each actual provider call. Codex receives only a random opaque `127.0.0.1` route: selected credential values, their configured environment names, and inherited aliases containing those values are removed from its process. The broker pins the exact approved HTTPS endpoint, strips client authorization, injects approved bearer/environment headers outside Codex, rejects redirects and upstream authentication challenges, bounds transport, and exact-redacts allowed headers plus buffered/SSE bodies before they reach the model.
- Restored ordinary persistent-session behavior for authenticated selected-Skill MCP routes. Direct calls, map packets, team turns, and guarded `recover-run --resume-codex` continuations now use the same UUID-bound semantics as unauthenticated routes, with a fresh capability route on every process invocation. No persistent broker, config, OAuth store, transcript, launcher, daemon, or repository-local state is added; ambient client OAuth cannot reach the upstream endpoint.
- Added provider-free adversarial coverage for exact target/header injection, client-auth stripping, raw/JSON-escaped response and header redaction, SSE chunk boundaries, redirect/auth/transport failure, custom timeout binding, stalled-client teardown, strict loopback config parsing, provider environment scrubbing, direct execution, actual same-thread checkpoint recovery, and authenticated team completion. Arbitrary transformed, encoded, or split output from the approved endpoint remains an explicit exact-redaction limitation.

## 0.149.0

- Added explicit profile-specific Skill entrypoint preloading. Operator-authored `conductor.agent_profile.v1` definitions may select up to eight canonical workspace-relative Skill directories; Conductor loads only each regular, symlink-free, non-empty UTF-8 `SKILL.md`, with 128 KiB per-entrypoint and 64-entry/256 KiB workflow limits. Model-authored workflows cannot self-select Skills, and omission performs no Skill lookup, read, prompt, cache, state, or command work.

## 0.146.0

- Added opt-in fail-closed `agent_stop` acceptance across direct `codex_exec`, uncached map packets, team planning/review, ordinary turns, and quality retries. `warn` remains the compatible default. Explicit `block` creates strict private `conductor.agent_lifecycle_stop_gate.v1` state only when a matching blocking hook exists; advisory-only and omitted configurations retain the prior no-gate fast path.
- Made the stop gate hard-crash conservative. It is fsynced as `pending` before provider launch, binds the exact content-free invocation and ordered warn/block hook set, stores the terminal-derived result before hook execution, durably claims one hook at a time, and records bounded hash-only results. Direct, map, and team terminal recovery continues only never-claimed hooks. A possibly executed hook becomes `uncertain` and rejects the provider result without hook or provider replay; failed, missing, tampered, symlinked, over-limit, cross-bound, or ambiguous evidence also fails closed. Completion-only team recovery requires an already passed gate.
- Added strict schema export and provider-free adversarial coverage for all six scopes, filters, mixed ordering, parallel packet isolation, plan/review, same-session quality retry, successful and blocking failures, attempt-renumbered terminal recovery, completion-only recovery, gate removal/tamper/symlink rejection, crash before claim, crash between hooks, crash after possible hook execution, and advisory no-artifact behavior. Blocking gates control Conductor result acceptance; they cannot roll back mutation already made by a direct shared-workspace provider, while isolated team writes remain unmerged until acceptance.

## 0.142.0

- Added strict `conductor.agent_lifecycle_hook_input.v1` stdin and schema export. The envelope carries bounded invocation identity, topology, budget, session mode, and hashes of workflow/model/prompt/session/output/provider streams, never prompt text, provider output, raw model/session values, commands, or paths. Invocation-keyed logs cannot collide under parallel maps, state recording is serialized, redaction and output limits remain authoritative, and omission bypasses payload construction with zero hook process or model call.
- Kept recovery semantics conservative. `agent_start` defaults to fail-closed blocking before provider launch. `agent_stop` defaults to and requires advisory `warn` because a hard crash can recover terminal provider evidence without safely replaying a post-result side effect. Lifecycle commands are local/read-only, cannot request write, destructive, network, or external-path authority, cannot use shared captures or automatic retry, and execute in the exact provider workspace. Durable blocking stop/continuation receipts, lifecycle context injection, and tool-level interception remain explicit follow-on gaps.

## 0.141.0

- Added opt-in event wake to model-selected adaptive goal intervals. `run-model-goal --monitor-command-json` requires `--dynamic-interval`, treats the model-selected delay as a deadline, and wakes on the first non-empty stdout line from one no-shell, secret-screened, policy-classified read-only command. Network and external-path authority remain explicit; writes and destructive commands are rejected. The isolated child has bounded output/event capture and is killed as a process group after event or deadline.
- Added fail-closed private monitor receipts and replay-safe recovery. Event text is redacted, bounded, framed as untrusted planner feedback, and exposed publicly only by lifecycle, counts, and hashes. Timeout performs the normal retry; nonzero or eventless exit stops before another planner call. Interruption while active becomes `uncertain` on resume, never relaunches automatically, and waits only the remaining persisted deadline. Raw argv crosses a detached launch only through anonymous stdin and never enters external metadata.
- Added foreground/background/dashboard visibility, strict state and handoff binding, policy/failure/tamper/interruption tests, and a 147th packaged interface check. Omission preserves the prior dynamic-wait shape and adds no provider call, polling loop, daemon, restart policy, cloud trigger, or general streaming UI.
- Shipped and installed exact `0.141.0`. ## 0.140.0

- Added opt-in model-selected retry intervals to adaptive goals. `run-model-goal --dynamic-interval` requires one model-only verifier and extends that existing fail-closed call with a strict next-delay choice, so interval selection adds no provider call. Operator bounds default to 1-60 minutes and may narrow but not widen that range; satisfied verdicts schedule nothing, while malformed, boolean, missing-reason, unknown-field, or out-of-range choices stop before another iteration.
- Added interruption-safe waiting for foreground and detached goals. Each false verdict atomically persists the exact policy, selected delay, reason hash/count, selection time, and absolute UTC wake time before sleeping. Matching resume reuses that wake time without model reselection, elapsed waits never replay, and verdict/reason/timestamp/payload/policy drift fails closed. Background heartbeats, signal cleanup, status, and termination remain active during the wait; no daemon, restart policy, service, or new capability is introduced.
- Added bounded dynamic-wait visibility to goal state and static/live dashboard summaries, strict anonymous-pipe configuration binding for detached workers, five focused provider-free tests, and a packaged CLI parity check. Existing immediate goals retain their exact four-field verdict and command/composite behavior.
- Shipped and installed exact `0.140.0`. ## 0.139.0

- Added strict five-field numeric cron schedules to routine creation and approved schedule replacement. The dependency-free parser accepts wildcards, values, comma lists, ascending ranges, and positive steps; normalizes whitespace and decimal spelling; maps day-of-week `0` and `7` to Sunday; implements Vixie's leading-wildcard day-mask rule plus OR semantics when neither day field begins with `*`; and rejects names, extensions, macros, seconds, non-ASCII digits, malformed ranges/steps, out-of-range values, and expressions over 128 characters.
- Added bounded timezone-aware cron due-slot resolution shared by transient supervisors and restart-persistent services. The scheduler searches only real UTC minute instants in the existing seven-day latest-slot window, skips nonexistent spring-forward minutes, treats repeated fall-back minutes as two distinct slots, respects manifest creation and prior scheduled instants, and never replays a consumed slot. Fifty maximally sparse routines scan the complete window in about 0.20 seconds on the release host.
- Extended the strict routine manifest schema, schedule labels/status, `write-routine-manifest --cron`, and `update-routine-schedule --cron`. Thirteen focused provider-free tests cover canonicalization, malformed syntax, schema, CLI approval, Vixie matching, Sunday aliases, catch-up, replay, creation bounds, timezones, both DST transitions, direct supervision, durable service execution, and packaged self-launch authority. All 863 warning-strict tests pass before packaging; no model or provider call was made.
- Fixed installed/plugin routine portability: manifests written by a `.pyz` now invoke that exact absolute runtime instead of assuming `conductor_runtime` is importable from the scheduled workspace. The manifest binds the runtime SHA-256 and rejects drift, while strict cross-field validation prevents launch argv from changing target, workspace, runs directory, worker ceiling, or capability policy. Legacy source-module manifests remain valid.
- Shipped and installed exact `0.139.0`. - Added mode-`0700` notification sidecars for external goal and pre-run wrapper artifacts while retaining the strict mode-`0600` `conductor.desktop_notification.v1` receipt. Sidecars reject symlinks, contain no path or execution identity, reuse the existing atomic pre-send claim and uncertain-interruption rules, and normalize terminal goal/wrapper statuses into the fixed blocked/completed/failed/stopped vocabulary without accepting active states.
- Added `write-routine-manifest --desktop-notify`. In-process delivery starts after the routine timer is disabled and cannot change workflow or routine outcome.

Expanded focused coverage from 26 to 39 tests and the packaged parity matrix from 136 to 142 checks without adding a model/provider call.

## 0.137.0

- Added explicit `--desktop-notify` support to `run`, `run-saved-workflow`, and `start-background-run`. Notifications contain only a fixed `Codex Conductor` title and one fixed blocked/completed/failed/stopped sentence. Task text, output, paths, errors, model text, secrets, workflow name, and run identity never enter backend argv or receipts. Omission creates no receipt and launches no notification process; dry-run requests are rejected.
- Added strict exactly-once `conductor.desktop_notification.v1` receipts. A mode-`0600` per-status `sending` claim is created atomically before backend launch, final claims suppress replay, concurrent callers cannot duplicate the OS command, and an interrupted claim becomes `uncertain` without automatic retry. Separate status files allow a blocked run and its later approved completion to notify independently.
- Bound local delivery to fixed trusted executables with no shell, null stdio, and a five-second timeout: `/usr/bin/osascript` on macOS and root-owned, non-group/world-writable `/usr/bin/notify-send` on Linux. Missing, nonzero, timeout, receipt, or backend errors are advisory and cannot change workflow status or a completed foreground/detached exit. Detached argv persists only the boolean flag and no approval values.
- Added strict receipt loading and cross-field validation, public `desktop-notification` JSON Schema export, read-only `validate-desktop-notification`, and focused coverage for privacy, fixed paths/content, foreground/saved/detached propagation, blocked and completed outcomes, omission, concurrency, replay, interruption, timeout, tamper, symlink rejection, schema, and command-policy behavior. Goal loops, model-workflow wrappers, routine supervisors/services, and cloud tasks remain explicitly outside this release's notification scope.
- Shipped and installed exact `0.137.0`. The same check runs during terminal recovery and rejects a completed terminal overage; unavailable reconciliation remains advisory. Regression coverage proves a measured 1,201/1,200 provider-success overage cannot become a completed run.

## 0.118.0

- Fixed Claude cutoff answer selection. A non-empty terminal `result` remains authoritative; when a budget or turn cutoff leaves it empty, the strict stream parser now uses only the last non-empty completed assistant message. Multiple text blocks within that message retain order, while earlier progress narration remains counted but is not concatenated into the captured or scored answer. This adds no task-specific parser, provider call, retry, permission, turn, or budget.
- Kept execution truth separate from retained quality. A valid recovered final message may receive its deterministic quality score, but a provider error, model rejection, timeout, truncation, or cap overshoot still leaves provider and final success false. ## 0.117.0

- Added `run-goal --workflow-completion`, a zero-process, zero-provider verifier that reuses the workflow's existing `completion_verdict: strict-v1`. Preflight requires exactly one verdict step and proves that it transitively depends on every other workflow step, so an early or parallel review cannot become authoritative. The mode is mutually exclusive with command and model verifiers; omission preserves existing behavior.
- Bound local verification and resume to the exact post-resource-binding workflow fingerprint, terminal step id, verdict contract, completed run state, state metrics, and one regular no-follow output snapshot. A valid false verdict still drives the existing private bounded repair path without running a verifier; a valid true verdict records only confidence, evidence count, feedback presence, output size/hash, and `provider_calls: 0`. Missing, malformed, unsatisfied, changed, duplicated, nonterminal, or topology-drifted evidence fails closed.
- Updated generated-model guidance to exact prompt contract `conductor.model_workflow_prompt.v5`: planners can make the final verdict authoritative only by placing one strict verdict after every other step in the dependency graph. Current receipt validation retains v4 compatibility, while legacy v3 receipts reject v4/v5. Dashboard and goal views expose only fixed hash/count evidence. Exact subcommand help such as `run-goal --help` is now classified read-only without weakening ordinary runtime execution policy.

## 0.116.0

- Added zero-overhead-on-success verdict-driven goal repair. When a `run-goal` or `run-model-goal` iteration ends on exactly one valid unsatisfied `completion_verdict: strict-v1`, the failed step and run remain failed, the external verifier is skipped, and only the bounded redacted private feedback is framed as untrusted input for the next already-authorized iteration. Ordinary `run`, omitted verdicts, and first-pass success are unchanged. Invalid, satisfied, missing, multiple, changed, over-limit, or otherwise inconsistent verdict evidence never enters the repair path.
- Made repair resumable without making feedback public. Goal state and static/live detail retain only strict `conductor.completion_verdict_feedback.v1` fields: step/contract, confidence, evidence count, feedback presence/length/hash, and output size/hash. Resume derives the expected run id from goal identity, then revalidates the redacted copied workflow, original workflow fingerprint, failed state metrics, exact private artifact, parsed false verdict, and complete goal receipt before recovering text. `run-model-goal` feeds the same private result to its next planner turn; current architect prompts bind new exact contract `conductor.model_workflow_prompt.v4`, while legacy v3 receipts remain valid only with v3.
- Closed a verdict TOCTOU defect in `0.115.0`: acceptance previously hashed and parsed through two file opens. The runtime now derives UTF-8 decoding, strict parsing, byte count, and SHA-256 from one regular no-follow snapshot. Dashboard revalidation uses the same shared loader. Malformed bounded output still retains a hash receipt, while unreadable or oversized output remains invalid without a second snapshot.

## 0.115.0

- Closed the semantic-success gap in model-backed workflows. A successful `codex_exec` process can now opt into `completion_verdict: strict-v1`, which appends a fixed, prompt-hash-bound review contract and accepts only one bounded JSON object with exactly `satisfied`, `feedback`, `evidence`, and `confidence`. The shared parser rejects duplicate keys, non-finite constants, unknown or missing fields, oversized values, evidence-free success, and feedback-free failure. The field is valid only for read-only `codex_exec` steps; omission preserves existing behavior and adds no provider call.
- Verdict handling is fail-closed in both the ordinary return path and strict terminal recovery. Provider success and telemetry are accounted separately from semantic acceptance; malformed or unsatisfied output marks the step and run failed without retrying or launching downstream work. Satisfied recovery remains zero-call. Generated Ultracode final review now receives synthesis, implementation, and verification artifacts through the existing hash-bound dependency handoff and automatically uses the strict verdict contract. Model-authored workflows may request the same bounded field.
- Kept review content private while making acceptance auditable. Run state stores only contract, validity, satisfaction, confidence, evidence count, feedback presence, output size, and SHA-256. Static/live detail independently reopens and rehashes the workflow-bound output, suppresses the verdict artifact and provider logs from generic excerpts, and reports drift as invalid. Diagnostics surface actionable invalid or unsatisfied status without echoing feedback or evidence text.

## 0.114.0

- Fixed a structural fan-out/fan-in defect in generated Ultracode workflows: `depends_on` ordered packet review, synthesis, implementation, verification, and final review but never transferred the prior artifacts into later model prompts. New `codex_exec.context_from` performs that handoff explicitly without another planner or provider call. Generated context mapping now receives collected files and reproduction output; analysis receives context plus raw reproduction evidence; synthesis receives analysis plus every bound packet result; implementation receives synthesis; and final review receives synthesis, implementation, then verification evidence.
- Kept the transfer bounded and fail-closed. Only one through 32 unique direct `write_artifact`, captured `shell`, `codex_exec`, or `agent_map` dependencies are valid. Dynamic maps require a statically provable packet ceiling and the combined upper bound must fit 32 artifacts before any workflow process starts. Referenced single-output producers alone compute hash/size receipts; maps reuse their complete workflow/generation/prompt/source/sandbox/model/output cache identity. Consumers require completed rather than skipped producers, then hash and excerpt each regular no-follow artifact from one descriptor under a 2 MiB file ceiling, an 8 KiB excerpt ceiling, and a 64 KiB aggregate ceiling. Missing receipts, stale or uncacheable map sources, count overflow, symlinks, non-files, size/content drift, and oversize fail before the downstream provider launches. Omission preserves the previous zero-receipt path.
- Dependency content is labeled untrusted, secret-redacted again, stripped of exact run paths, and protected against nested section/source-marker injection. Framing exposes only source step id, ordinal, and output hash. Exact section bytes enter the ordinary prompt/checkpoint/continuation/terminal binding; state and static/live/API run detail retain only fixed contract id, source/artifact counts, byte count, and SHA-256. The public workflow schema, model-authored planner allowlist/prompt, runtime documentation, installable Skill reference, and a bundled validation workflow describe the same contract.
- Added 14 focused tests covering zero-overhead omission, direct/source-kind/list/artifact-bound validation, dynamic-map preflight, schema export, raw reproduction routing, shell receipts, map-to-synthesis-to-implementation propagation, all-source aggregate retention, redaction, section/source marker injection, exact run-path removal, hash-only dashboard summaries, missing receipts, workspace drift, output tampering, and symlink substitution. All 782 tests pass with warnings treated as errors; all 18 workflows and 81 source JSON files validate. Local text/security audit, official Skill validation, archive integrity, isolated dry-run/install/idempotent reinstall, guarded active upgrade from `0.113.0`, no-approval active idempotent reinstall, and active host doctor pass. ## 0.113.0

- Superseded the insufficient final-answer-only native policy with `parent-integration-and-synthesis-v2`. Exact-build `0.112.0` evidence showed the child consuming the shared budget before repository inspection while the parent waited, then emitting only a protocol-valid 2/10 residual-risk answer. Native guidance now forbids delegating the whole task, requires the parent to inspect a complementary file group immediately after spawn, and keeps the parent doing useful work while the child runs.
- The existing 50%-remaining reminder is now a mandatory native integration stop: no new child work, integrate an already available result, otherwise interrupt or close the child without waiting, and permit at most one targeted direct inspection of a critical missing source. The one-third-remaining checkpoint, capped at 6,000 tokens, remains the no-tools final-synthesis stop. Both checkpoint integers and fixed policy id are visible in state, workflow inspection, static/live detail, and missing-answer diagnostics. The hard shared cap, reminder mechanism, call count, effort, child authority, retry behavior, and permissions remain unchanged.
- Expanded focused tests to require complementary parent work, whole-task delegation refusal, the exact integration/synthesis schedule, interruption without waiting, state/UI visibility, and compatibility with strict failed-turn output recovery. Implementation and release verification launched no provider.

## 0.112.0

- Added `parent-synthesis-checkpoint-v1` for explicitly authorized native Codex turns after the exact-build `0.111.0` cohort showed one child consuming the shared 18,000-token threshold before the parent emitted any answer. The runtime deterministically schedules an additional reminder at one-third of the effective cap, capped at 6,000 weighted tokens remaining. From that checkpoint the parent is instructed to stop child and shell/collaboration work, integrate available evidence, and emit the requested answer immediately. The existing 90%, 50%, and 10% reminders remain; no cap, provider call, retry, continuation, effort, permission, or child slot was added.
- This is intentionally not described as a hard per-session token reservation because Codex exposes one provider-owned parent/child rollout budget. Run state records only the fixed policy id and checkpoint integer. Workflow inspection, static and live detail show the checkpoint; a native budget failure with no recoverable parent answer emits action-required `native_parent_answer_missing` guidance to prefer serial routing or narrow delegated scope. Existing failed-turn recovery remains authoritative when an answer was emitted.
- Added focused tests for the exact reminder schedule, prompt contract, state fields, static/live visibility, cap-exhaustion diagnosis, ordinary failed-output compatibility, and the existing native authority envelope. Implementation and release verification launched no provider.

Malformed, truncated, unterminated, oversized, or ambiguous streams synthesize no output.
- Failed-step state remains content-free and records only stream validity, terminal class, budget-exhaustion marker, preservation marker, fixed source class, byte count, and SHA-256. Static/live detail independently rehashes the workflow-bound no-follow artifact and reports `valid`, `invalid`, or `none`; diagnostics make drift action-required. ## 0.110.0

- Added a separate objective read-only evidence campaign rather than weakening the write-capable parity or auto-topology contracts. `conductor.readonly_parity_campaign.v1` preregisters three diagnosis tasks over repeated balanced `serial-codex`, `native-codex`, and `claude-sonnet` arms, hashes the complete task and rendered provider contract, and gives every arm an independently copied identical source snapshot. The public `readonly-parity-campaign` schema, planning/writing/validation/status commands, and provider-free dry-run launch no model.
- Both Codex arms now use the same caller-fixed `gpt-5.6-sol` effort and 18,000-weighted-token runtime termination threshold. Serial carries no native authority; native carries exactly one depth-one child slot. A new optional direct-workflow threshold exists only for explicit callers, rejects a native value that differs from the derived shared threshold, and leaves the ordinary 12,000-token direct default unchanged. The content-free rollout reconciler is also exposed under a topology-neutral session-usage name so zero-child serial and parent-plus-child native totals use one accounting contract.
- Added `tools/evaluate_readonly_diagnostic.py` and `benchmark-suites/read-only-diagnostic-tasks.json`. Providers must return bounded strict JSON findings. The evaluator matches file, first-faulty-line, and root-cause concepts against a versioned key held outside provider workspaces, penalizes false positives, and persists only task/source/answer/key hashes, matched identifiers, bounded counts, criterion scores, and pass state. Raw answer text remains in private arm artifacts and never enters public status.
- `run-readonly-parity-arm` narrows effective capabilities per system, keeps all arms read-only, forces Claude through the strict Sonnet Ultracode adapter with no fallback or Opus main response, and advances durable preparing/ready/launching/captured/finalized state. Campaigns and results now bind an exact runtime-build hash in addition to the semantic version, and a mismatched build fails before provider discovery or launch receipt creation. A terminal captured artifact may resume deterministic finalization; an unknown interrupted provider outcome is never replayed. A bounded answer emitted before a failed Codex terminal event can be recovered only from the strict hash-bound JSONL stream and scored without converting provider failure to success. Failed providers, malformed answers, unavailable telemetry, unchanged-source failures, and native arms that used no child remain visible scored coverage.
- `status-readonly-parity-campaign` independently validates task/source/provider/workflow/run/progress/stream/answer/evaluation hashes and schemas, then reports quality, final success, source preservation, native-child compliance, raw latency, provider-native gross tokens, comparable Codex weighted tokens, authoritative Claude cost, cap-observation coverage, compliance, and measured overshoot separately. Pairwise output also reports final-success-first duration and gross tokens to success, so an early failed arm cannot win efficiency merely by stopping cheaply. Every result derives nullable compliance and overshoot from observed weighted tokens or provider cost; an observed breach forces provider failure. Live completion output now shows provider success, duration, cap evidence, and observed weighted tokens or cost immediately. Quality advantages require complete repeated coverage and paired Wilson uncertainty; native routing additionally requires observed child use, complete aggregate Codex and cap accounting, and no breach. Unequal provider-dollar and weighted-token thresholds remain explicit, Codex dollar cost remains unavailable, and universal superiority is permanently false for this read-only cohort.
- The first paid preliminary serial canary was deliberately retained as a counterexample and stopped the sequence before any native or Claude spend. `gpt-5.6-sol` ultra emitted a complete strict answer, then exhausted the 18,000 weighted-token threshold after 110.769 seconds. Local reconciliation observed 115,805 input, 95,488 cached input, 4,067 output, 119,872 gross, and 24,384 weighted tokens: a 6,384-token overshoot. The original runner retained provider failure but lost the final answer because Codex wrote no final-message file. This release adds strict partial-answer recovery and explicit overshoot accounting; it does not relabel the preliminary arm or call an in-flight threshold an absolute spend-prevention guarantee.
- A fresh exact-build campaign completed one three-arm event-routing cohort without invalid evidence. Serial `gpt-5.6-sol` ultra was the only final success: score 9/10, source preserved, 126.013 seconds, 69,753 gross and 16,505 weighted tokens, with zero overshoot. One-child native found every root cause and scored 10/10 in 47.344 seconds, but 21,228 weighted tokens crossed the matched threshold by 3,228, so provider and final success remained false despite the retained answer. Claude was command-pinned to `claude-sonnet-5` Ultracode, observed one Haiku helper and no Opus, reached eight turns and `$0.3253611` against `$0.25`, and retained only non-conforming partial output for score 0 after 169.161 seconds and 56,115 gross tokens. The cohort was bound to release-candidate runtime SHA-256 `fa045b8690d2b7a00433e5dd5da917d66344ab158fa0a31a25d23b1d733c69c1`; subsequent provider-free changes only improve live summaries and success-conditioned comparison. Five cohorts remain unrun, both unequal thresholds were breached, and no routing, broad-quality, cost, or universal claim is supported.
- The provider-free smoke matrix contains 119 checks, including the new fixture, schema, and balanced 18-arm campaign planner. All 764 tests pass with warnings treated as errors. - Added bounded content-free native Codex usage reconciliation after successful explicitly delegated steps. The hardened live `0.108.0` canary independently reconciles to its previously derived 2 sessions, 1 child, 55,673 gross tokens, and 15,993 weighted tokens.
- The reconciler queries only thread id, rollout path, workspace, gross total, and spawn edges; accepts only no-follow rollout paths beneath `CODEX_HOME/sessions`; bounds each file at 512 MiB and each tail search at 8 MiB; and parses only a candidate token-count line no larger than 256 KiB. Prompt, message, reasoning, command, output, tool, preview, role, nickname, identity, and path data is never retained, hashed, logged, or exposed. Missing, locked, changed, mismatched, nested, excessive, malformed, or incomplete local metadata reports unavailable and cannot alter execution success.

## 0.108.0

- Added explicit bounded native Codex delegation to ordinary read-only `codex_exec` steps and the zero-planner `auto --strategy native` route. The exact `native_agents.max_threads` authority permits one to six concurrently open depth-1 children, keeps the parent responsible for integration, rejects maps, writes, adaptive verifiers, isolated/restricted profiles, recursive fan-out, and model-authored self-grant, and requires `--allow-agent --allow-parallel --approve native-agent-delegation` before execution. Auto defaults to two children and derives one shared parent-plus-child hard ceiling of `12,000 + 6,000 * child_slots` weighted tokens.
- Enforced native concurrency across both supported Codex contracts: legacy child capacity is `N`, current total capacity is `N + 1`, and depth remains one. Native calls mechanically disable irrelevant plugin, app, browser, computer, MCP, web, hook, goal, memory, dependency, and general fan-out surfaces while preserving repository guidance, the selected model, and the standard local shell path. A prompt-only preflight on Codex 0.144.1 confirms a one-child request exposes exactly two total slots and reduces the model-visible preamble from 13,656 to 7,834 bytes.
- Added current `conductor.auto_orchestration_receipt.v2`, deterministic-v4 routing, model-workflow receipt v4 native-direct provenance, and `conductor.codex_progress.v3`. V1 auto receipts, v3-v1 model-workflow receipts, and v2/v1 progress remain strict compatibility exports. Run state, console, static dashboard, and live dashboard expose native limits while explicitly retaining incomplete lifecycle and nested-usage attribution.
- Clarified every native budget display as a shared weighted rollout cap and every progress total as gross provider telemetry. Current v4 evidence already computes status and overshoot from non-cached input plus output; gross-token comparisons remain confined to strict historical-schema compatibility.
- Paid diagnostic canaries exposed and preserved the original 12,000-token shared-budget failure before the contract changed. ## 0.90.0

Current v4 receipts retain only the resolved-path hash, bounded tracked-content fingerprint, file/byte counts, and excluded-directory count/hash; raw paths and file contents are never persisted. - `run-reviewed-model-workflow` now verifies both the exact graph/receipt and the bound workspace path/content before creating run evidence. V3 and explicitly unbound v4 plans remain usable only through `--allow-unbound-workspace`; real execution additionally requires `--approve unbound-reviewed-workspace`, while dry-run can preflight the override without execution approval.

Strict universal inference remains unchanged and still reports raw latency, cost, and token outcomes. ## 0.77.0

- Added a dependency-free release-bundle installer. `release-manifest.json` binds the semantic version, runtime and installer bytes, and every text-only Skill path, size, and SHA-256. `install.py --dry-run` validates the complete bundle without writes; first install requires `--allow-writes --approve conductor-install`; replacing any differing release, runtime, or Skill additionally requires `--replace --approve conductor-update`; identical reruns are no-write successes.
- Installation now stages and revalidates versioned plus active copies under configured external Codex/Conductor homes, rejects path escape, symlinked destination components, symlinked or unmanifested Skill content, and malformed/tampered manifests, and restores prior targets after a caught multi-target commit failure. It never edits repositories, PATH, shell startup, services, schedulers, or approval values. The release bundle remains dependency-free and under 25 MiB.
- Replaced every deprecated `datetime.utcnow()` and `datetime.utcfromtimestamp()` call with one Python 3.9-compatible UTC boundary while preserving existing naive-UTC arithmetic and persisted `Z` formats. All 643 tests pass on Python 3.14 with `DeprecationWarning` promoted to an error, including clean install, idempotency, tamper rejection, duplicate-key rejection, replacement gating, symlink rejection, rollback, executable runtime, and reproducible bundle coverage.
- All 14 bundled workflows validate; source, extracted-bundle, isolated-installed, and active-installed smoke matrices each pass 71/71. Two independent runtime, bundle, manifest, and Skill builds were byte-identical. SHA-256 values are `05d35b18b32b53e045ab93ccda95bd45779b4307ef76661cfc5044dede500c4e` for the runtime, `7cb66df047f3b04b98444512dc531070c2418fd15a91a50ff66c813610f094f7` for the bundle, `70baff867d46e395a4072dc5fddb0bdc4cd9f1bfc458794a6e3e5358d9c12d21` for the release manifest, and `22ec3181b05800afeb0fa009a1595b84f71105fdfb3caa14fa58c2188e8cc6dd` for the Skill archive. ## 0.69.0

- Executed the first preregistered high-effort campaign row exactly once in its Codex-then-Claude order. Both providers scored 10/10, completed normally, and had no actionable safety incident. Codex used 23,601 gross tokens versus Claude's 53,074, but took 51.786 seconds versus 27.946. Claude was pinned to Sonnet Ultracode, resolved `claude-sonnet-5` plus one Haiku helper, observed no Opus, and cost `$0.0927103` against its `$0.25` cap. The row is therefore a quality/execution/safety tie, Codex token win, and Claude latency win.
- Added conservative `auto` effort resolution. An omitted `--planner-effort` now resolves to `medium` only for direct or progressive work with an explicit verifier, at most 1,000 task characters, and no broad, sensitive, migration, refactor, test-authoring, concurrency, schema, or repository-scale marker. Every unverified, plan-first, decomposed, long, or marked task remains `high`; explicit `low|medium|high|xhigh|ultra` always wins. Receipts retain the actual resolved effort rather than the `auto` label, and task text still cannot select topology or grant capabilities.
- Removed recursive orchestration and redundant verification from deterministic direct workers. Their prompt now treats the runtime call as the complete workflow, forbids opening external skills/plugins/goals or assuming Git, and relies on the already configured external verifier. Auto-selected medium verified writes receive one combined pre-edit read; high verified work may use two reads in compact workspaces and additional focused reads in larger repositories; `xhigh` and `ultra` remain unrestricted. Unverified writes retain one focused existing check.
- A real pre-fix generic-auto slug probe retained a correct patch but failed after 120.553 seconds because it opened the Conductor Skill plus five references, attempted Git, tried two Python entry points, and ran repeated bespoke checks until the 24,000-token cap. After the complete-workflow contract, a second probe completed in 26.318 seconds but used 61,919 gross tokens over two discovery reads. The final one-read probe completed in 20.529 seconds with 47,140 gross tokens and passed all 3 visible plus 5 held-out tests. Against the fresh Sonnet row, that compatibility sample was 7.417 seconds faster and used 5,934 fewer gross tokens at equal 10/10 quality.
- Preserved hard-task quality with a real eight-file quota auto probe. The selector retained `high`; the compact two-read contract completed normally in 62.564 seconds with 69,508 gross tokens and passed all 5 visible plus 8 held-out tests. Against the fresh quota Sonnet row, this separate compatibility sample was 13.526 seconds faster, used 11,869 fewer gross tokens, and scored 10/10 versus 5/10. These cross-run probes motivate the policy but are not randomized campaign or causal evidence.
- Deterministic command verification may now accept a terminal failed write workflow when the retained workspace passes exactly. The iteration still records `run_status: failed`; only write-capable runs with a real run directory and command-only verifier qualify. Blocked, interrupted, missing-run, read-only, and model-verifier outcomes retain their prior fail-closed behavior, while a failed check remains bounded retry feedback.
- The new high-effort campaign is 1/15 complete with no partial or invalid rows. Broad and universal superiority remain false pending repeated paired evidence, cap-stratification completion, and comparable cost telemetry.
- The full suite has 633 passing tests, all 14 bundled workflows validate, and source, correctly configured extracted-bundle, and installed-runtime matrices each have 68/68 passing smoke checks. ## 0.65.0

- Fixed the interactive Codex integration failure shown in the command-host screenshot. The standalone `codex` launcher had been linked into `~/.local/bin` without its required sibling `codex-code-mode-host`; the sibling now resolves through `standalone/current` to the signed OpenAI 0.144.0 release.
- Expanded `doctor` from a launcher-only check to strict companion-host diagnostics with bounded JSON output. It detects missing, broken, non-executable, source-unavailable, and release-mismatched hosts. Explicit `--repair-codex-host --approve codex-host-repair` creates only a missing sibling symlink under the user home, is idempotent when healthy, and never overwrites an existing entry.
- Classified repair mode as write-capable while keeping plain `doctor` read-only. The Skill now stops immediately after an explicit transport failure instead of retrying the same unavailable command host and consuming another model turn.
- Verified the repaired route with a fresh ephemeral `gpt-5.6-sol` low-effort turn: Codex launched `/bin/zsh -lc pwd` through code mode, captured the correct working directory, and completed normally in 6.2 seconds with no missing-host error.

## 0.64.0

- Added strict `conductor.claude_provider_evidence.v2` measured-token evidence. The parser now aggregates every main and helper `modelUsage` record into uncached input, cache-creation input, cache-read input, output, and gross total tokens under explicit `provider-native-gross-v1` accounting. Counters must be complete, non-negative, bounded, and arithmetically consistent or the stream fails closed; wholly absent counters remain explicitly unavailable. Raw stream events and model-specific records are still not persisted.
- Preserved strict v1 compatibility with a separate validator path, public schema, and template. Current read-only and staged Claude calls emit v2; benchmark reports, live manifests, campaign rows, dashboards, and comparison validation accept both exact versions without silently rewriting historical artifacts.
- Upgraded campaign status to `conductor.parity_campaign_status.v3`. Cost and token summaries now expose per-system observed totals, paired coverage, lower-is-better Codex/Claude wins and ties, and a named token-accounting basis. Token pairs count as comparable only when both sides use the same provider-native gross contract. Universal superiority now remains false when Claude wins any comparable cost or token row; mere measurement completeness can no longer satisfy a resource dimension.
- Ran one controlled no-tool, one-turn Claude Code 2.1.206 schema probe pinned to Sonnet Ultracode with no fallback. It observed `claude-sonnet-5` plus a Haiku helper and no Opus, stopped at `$0.0208987` against a `$0.02` cap, and exposed 2,465 uncached input, 1,119 cache-creation, 3,289 cache-read, and 463 output tokens, totaling 7,336. The captured stream replays into valid v2 budget-exceeded evidence without another provider call.
- The full suite has 624 passing tests, all 14 bundled workflows validate, and source, extracted-bundle, and installed-runtime matrices each have 66/66 passing smoke checks. Two independent builds were byte-identical, active and archived runtime bytes match, the installed Skill matches the text-only source, the local security audit is clean, and no repository-local Conductor state exists.

## 0.63.0

- Completed the fifteenth and final preregistered implementation-canary row, `r003-quota-ledger-contract`, exactly once in its stored Codex-then-Claude order under installed v0.62. Codex changed both required modules, passed 5 visible and 8 held-out tests, and scored 10/10; Claude passed visible verification but missed malformed-ledger-constructor and reservation-object type contracts in held-out evaluation and scored 5/10. Claude was forced to Sonnet Ultracode, observed `claude-sonnet-5` with a Haiku helper and no Opus, finished in 61.528 seconds, and reported `$0.2063888` against its `$0.20` request. Codex took 216.846 seconds. Both providers reached their native caps, so execution, final success, and actionable safety tied while Codex won quality and Claude won latency.
- Campaign evidence is complete at 15/15 with no partial or invalid rows. Codex leads aggregate quality 92/150 to 74/150, but pairwise quality is five Codex wins, six Claude wins, and four ties. Claude leads execution/final success two to zero with thirteen ties, latency eight to seven and by 332.151 seconds in aggregate, and actionable safety five to four with six ties. Codex's paired mean quality advantage is 12 percentage points, but its confidence interval crosses zero. Cost/token mechanisms remain incomparable, broad superiority is unsupported, and universal superiority is false.
- Added a Codex-staged-only write-progress checkpoint at the existing 50%-remaining runtime reminder. If an edit task has not produced a required write by then, the worker must stop discovery and speculative audit and issue the best complete contract-mapped write immediately; the remaining half is reserved for still-unwritten affected files, a specific known gap, or failed-write correction. The first write may not be deferred to the final 10% reserve.
- The checkpoint responds to two consecutive capped Codex rows whose only writes landed in their final seconds. It does not lower the token cap or reasoning effort, change ordinary workers or Claude prompts, add a provider call, planner, retry, permission, hidden-test access, source mutation, or automatic apply, or weaken the deterministic verifier. Completed campaign evidence remains immutable.
- Ran one separate exact-profile v0.63 Codex quota compatibility probe. It completed normally in 147.509 seconds with no provider errors, used 18,719/24,000 weighted rollout tokens, passed visible verification, and independently scored 10/10 across all 5 visible and 8 held-out tests. Relative to the immediately preceding same-task campaign call, it was 69.337 seconds faster and used 5,281 fewer rollout tokens before the hard cap, but its writes still landed near the end of the turn. This single cross-run observation is not a causal latency estimate or campaign evidence.
- The full suite has 624 passing tests, all 14 bundled workflows validate, and source, extracted-bundle, and installed-runtime matrices each have 65/65 passing smoke checks. Two independent release builds were byte-identical, the active and archived runtimes match, the installed Skill matches the text-only source, and no repository-local `.codex` or `.codex-conductor` state exists.

- Proved the v0.59 small-workspace packet was active by reconstructing both exact provider prompt hashes from the immutable source. Against the earlier same-task repetition, Codex duration fell from 116.716 to 37.033 seconds and stream events fell from 18 to 11 while retaining 10/10 quality. This is strong local efficiency evidence, not a causal or universal claim; Claude duration and cost increased across repetitions.
- Isolated the remaining Codex completion loss to a contradictory post-edit instruction. Codex wrote the correct file about 16 seconds after launch, then spent about 21 seconds on the required static diff/whitespace phase; its retained stderr shows a post-edit host-initialized command failed through `xcode-select` immediately before token exhaustion.
- Replaced post-edit diff auditing with provider-neutral pre-write contract auditing and zero-tool finalization. Both staged wrappers now audit intended code while preparing required writes. Once all writes succeed, they forbid rereads, listings, diffs, checks, or explanatory tool calls, return one short completion sentence, and rely on the already authoritative external verifier plus deterministic completion summary. Multi-file writes and failed-write correction remain available until all required writes have succeeded.

## 0.59.0

- Executed preregistered row `r001-quota-ledger-contract` exactly once in its stored Codex-then-Claude order. Codex changed exactly `quota/parser.py` and `quota/ledger.py`, passed 5 visible and 8 held-out tests, scored 10/10, and finished in 71.277 seconds. Claude was forced to Sonnet Ultracode, observed `claude-sonnet-5` with a Haiku helper and no Opus, changed only `quota/parser.py`, failed verification, scored 1/10, finished in 93.176 seconds, and reported `$0.2394876` against the requested `$0.20` cap.
- Audited the Codex event and file-timestamp sequence. The provider copied its stage at launch, wrote the two correct files 89 milliseconds apart, and emitted its report 72 milliseconds after the second write, with no local test/runtime call or meaningful post-edit exploration. The remaining efficiency loss is pre-edit workspace discovery and reasoning, not verifier duplication after the patch.
- Added a provider-neutral small-workspace context path to both staged adapters. At most 24 files may be rendered once as canonical JSON after no-follow snapshot checks; both raw workspace bytes and serialized packet bytes must fit a 16 KiB ceiling further narrowed to half the applicable validated token ceiling. Filename, UTF-8, binary, framing-marker, and secret-like screens disable the entire packet; pre/post snapshot drift fails before provider launch. Repository bytes remain untrusted data, are bound by the existing provider-prompt hash, and are never copied into reports.
- Small safe stages now begin with complete file context and are told to avoid discovery-only listing/rereads before the first edit; target-only reads remain allowed when an edit tool requires them. Large or screened-out repositories retain the prior tool-driven path. No planner, retry, provider call, permission, background process, or automatic apply was added.
- Campaign coverage is now 11/15 with no partial or invalid rows. Quality is four Codex wins, five Claude wins, and two ties; execution/final success is one Claude win and ten ties; latency favors Codex six times and Claude five times; actionable safety is four wins each with three ties. Aggregate quality is 53/110 for Codex and 39/110 for Claude. Strict claim eligibility, broad superiority, and universal superiority remain false.
- The full suite has 623 passing tests, all 14 bundled workflows validate, and source, extracted-bundle, and installed-runtime matrices each have 64/64 passing smoke checks.
