## 0.52.0

- Added opt-in `on_failure: retry` for `team_task_created`, `team_task_completed`, and `team_member_idle` gates. Selected nonzero exits default to code 2 and can resume the same teammate session in the same execution workspace for one to four attempts; write teams retain the exact isolated member stage. Each retry has an optional narrower token cap and reserves from the existing aggregate team budget before launch. Omitted retry policy adds no call.
- Kept every candidate uncommitted until its fresh turn and all applicable gates pass. Timeout, policy denial, workspace mutation, an unlisted exit, attempt exhaustion, and insufficient aggregate budget remain blocking and never trigger a hidden provider call. Provider telemetry counts every actual attempt while accepted team state keeps one logical task turn.
- Added strict `conductor.agent_team_quality_retry.v1` pending/history checkpoints with separate current-retry and failed-event task identities, generation-scoped create-once retained outputs, and hashes for hook input, session, feedback, workspace, and retry output, but no raw feedback or session ID. Hard process loss never auto-replays a provider call; explicit `retry-step` verifies retained bytes, accepts only an outcome bound to the exact round/session/token/output team turn, otherwise records it abandoned and reconciles outstanding claims.
- Added read-only validation/inspection CLI, public schema, retry-indexed hook logs, report/metric fields, and static/live dashboard history and pending-recovery visibility. Tampered retained outputs fail before any resumed provider launch.
- Added success, exhaustion, budget, wrong-exit, timeout, mutation, same-stage write, same-session feedback, process-loss, explicit recovery, retained-output tamper, reset-generation isolation, CLI, policy, schema, and UI coverage. The full suite has 619 passing tests and the standalone source matrix has 64/64 passing smoke checks. No provider or paid Claude call was made; campaign evidence remains 4/15 and universal superiority remains false.

## 0.51.0

- Added optional deterministic agent-team quality gates for `team_task_created`, `team_task_completed`, and `team_member_idle`, with safe step/member/task filters, existing block/warn semantics, and policy-only dry-run preflight. Omitted hooks add no process or model call.
- Added strict `conductor.agent_team_hook_input.v1` stdin. It binds event/team/task identity, generation/round, turn and task hashes, workspace fingerprints, and bounded sorted changed paths without descriptions, summaries, messages, prompts, provider output, sessions, or approval values. The contract has a public schema and parity smoke check.
- Team gates now run after turn validation but before candidate state or source merge. Blocking failure discards the candidate, returns its task to pending, and supplies bounded redacted feedback to the next explicit retry; warning mode records and continues. No automatic model retry was introduced.
- Bound read-only gates to a fresh external source snapshot and write-team gates to the exact isolated member copy. Pre/post tracked-workspace fingerprints reject gate mutation regardless of warning mode. Unique event/step/generation/round/member/task logs and hash-only state/static/live evidence prevent repeated invocations from overwriting each other.
- Added strict/tamper, filter/policy, dry-run, dynamic-task event, explicit-retry feedback, warning, isolated-stage, mutation, resume-no-replay, schema, and UI coverage. The suite has 610 passing tests and 63 source parity smoke checks. No provider or paid Claude call was made; campaign evidence remains 4/15 and universal superiority remains false.

## 0.50.0

- Added a write-before-mutate barrier for accepted write-team results. Strict `conductor.agent_team_merge_transaction.v1` records bind identity, exact merge plan, source-before manifest, retained member workspace, complete candidate state/ledger, and every before/candidate/source hash before source can change.
- Added deterministic no-provider-replay recovery across every durable checkpoint: source before, partially applied, or complete; state before or candidate; and ledger before or candidate. Recovery applies only missing file operations, verifies the final source, commits candidate metadata, writes one idempotent `conductor.agent_team_merge_recovery.v1` receipt, removes the marker, and cleans retained workspace. Reset resolves the prior generation first; transaction/workspace/source/state/ledger tampering and unrelated drift fail closed.
- Added strict transaction/recovery validation and inspection commands, public schemas, read-only policy classification, pending/recovered static and live dashboard evidence, recovery metrics, and report counts. The guarantee begins after the pending transaction is durable; exact in-flight provider-turn recovery and the provider-result-before-marker window remain explicit gaps.
- Added crash injection after transaction prepare, source apply, state write, and ledger write; partial multi-file recovery; reset ordering; tamper/drift rejection; CLI/UI/schema/package coverage; and cumulative usage assertions. The suite now has 603 passing tests and 62 parity smoke checks.

## 0.49.0

- Added opt-in write-capable `agent_team` execution without changing the lightweight direct or read-only defaults. Every active teammate receives a fresh bounded symlink-free workspace copy under external run state; Codex is bound to that copy as both process cwd and `--cd`, so parallel members cannot race in the source repository.
- Added parent-owned `isolated-ordered-file-v1` merges for file additions, modifications, deletions, binary content, executable-bit changes, and directory-to-file replacement. Results are processed in stable team order. Identical same-path edits are deduplicated; different same-path edits reject the entire later result, leave only that task pending, and force its next round to run serially against a fresh copy of the merged source rather than using last-writer-wins.
- Added strict `conductor.agent_team_merge_ledger.v1` evidence with continuous source fingerprints, turn-output/delta/plan hashes, and changed/applied/deduplicated/conflicting path sets. Normal retry preserves accepted merges, completed resume revalidates the current source, and outside drift fails before another provider call. New validation/inspection commands, public schema, reports, metrics, and static/live dashboards expose bounded merge evidence without file contents.
- Allowed the strict model workflow architect to author isolated write teams only in a write-capable draft with `model-workflow-write` gate ancestry; `agent_map` remains read-only. Planner prompt contract v3 describes the merge semantics while earlier strict prompt/receipt contracts remain valid. Added `isolated-implementation-team.json` as an explicitly approved operator workflow.
- Fixed team usage accounting so repeated provider turns accumulate instead of replacing prior step usage; conflict-resolution calls now remain visible in final token totals. Added filesystem, merge, conflict, retry, drift, policy, planner, schema, CLI, UI, workflow, and standalone-smoke coverage. The suite now has 597 passing tests and 60 parity smoke checks. No provider or paid Claude call was made; campaign evidence remains 4/15 and universal superiority remains false.

## 0.48.0

- Closed the last internally constructed unbounded local `codex exec` path. Model and command-plus-model goal verifiers now use explicit `high` reasoning with an 8,000 weighted-token runtime-hard cap, an exact 4,000-token completion checkpoint, the strict isolated read-only/null-root profile, disabled alternate code/unified/deferred execution surfaces, and an ephemeral session. They no longer inherit user model effort, plugins, rules, project instructions, or a broken companion-host route merely to return the four-field verifier verdict.
- Bound the verifier execution policy into new goal fingerprints and persisted verifier metadata: effort, cap, runtime-hard enforcement, checkpoint, isolation, ephemeral-session use, and policy version. Every model-verifier result also records the same bounded policy beside usage and verdict evidence; cutoff, malformed output, timeout, or launch failure remains fail-closed.
- Preserved existing goal continuity without leaving a compatibility bypass. A saved pre-0.48 model or composite verifier fingerprint is accepted only as the one known legacy form for the same command/model/prompt. Resume records `verifier_policy_tightened`, rewrites the artifact to the new policy fingerprint and metadata before execution, and requires the new form thereafter. Unrelated fingerprint drift still fails before another provider call.
- Added verifier-policy summaries to goal collection, static goal detail, and live goal detail. Operators can see effort, maximum weighted tokens, cap enforcement, isolation, and ephemeral-session behavior without exposing semantic criteria or raw verifier output.
- Added command-envelope, prompt, result-policy, composite UI, and legacy-resume migration coverage. The suite now has 590 passing tests; no provider or paid Claude call was made, campaign evidence remains 4/15, and universal superiority remains false.

## 0.47.0

- Extended completion-reserve behavior from benchmark-only staged calls to ordinary `codex_exec`, `agent_map`, `agent_team`, interrupted-step resume, and read-only comparison prompts. Any worker with a configured weighted-token ceiling now treats the runtime's 50%-remaining reminder as a completion checkpoint and finalizes completed work instead of spending the reserve on optional exploration, repeated reads, broader checks, polishing, or explanation. Aggregate map/team allocation may lower the actual per-call cap, so ordinary prompts truthfully state the configured ceiling as an upper bound while runtime reminders remain authoritative.
- Added deterministic effort-derived model-architect budgets: `low` 4,000, `medium` 8,000, `high` 12,000, `xhigh` 16,000, and `ultra` 20,000 weighted tokens. Explicit higher reasoning effort still receives a larger allowance, but no model workflow planning turn is unbounded. Planner prompts receive the exact hard ceiling and reserve checkpoint.
- Moved model workflow architects onto the same strict read-only, null-root, host-independent Codex profile used by isolated workers. User config/rules/project instructions, network/web, plugins/apps, nested agents, code-mode hosts, unified execution, deferred execution, and adjacent optional surfaces are disabled while the minimal shell route remains available for workspace inspection. Planner session continuation remains supported.
- Upgraded planning evidence to `conductor.model_workflow_receipt.v3`. New receipts bind `planner_max_tokens`, runtime-hard versus not-applicable enforcement, completion-checkpoint use, and isolated-profile use. Deterministic direct routing records a zero planner cap and no planner call. Strict v1 and v2 receipts and public schemas remain supported.
- Added command-envelope, effort-cap, prompt, direct-zero-call, tamper, current/legacy schema, staged, ordinary-worker, and resume assertions. The suite remains at 589 passing tests and 56 source parity smoke checks. No provider or paid Claude call was made, and campaign evidence remains 4/15 with universal superiority false.

## 0.41.0

- Added opt-in per-profile `tool_policy: restricted` with strict structured `argv` exact rules, `argv_prefix` rules, and separately controlled `allow_apply_patch`. Rules are capped and schema/CLI validated; Bash input must be one expansion-free simple command, so compounds, substitutions, globbing, assignments, redirects, comments, controls, and malformed quoting fail closed.
- Built restricted execution on the existing minimal read-only/workspace-write permission envelope. It denies network/web, uses a fixed non-login sanitized shell environment with user startup/config roots redirected to the null device, ignores user Codex config and execpolicy rules, disables `unified_exec` plus alternate shell/code/plugin/app/browser/native-agent surfaces, and pins compatibility to Codex CLI `>=0.143.0,<0.144.0`.
- Added a self-contained policy hook whose canonical payload is SHA-256 bound into its command. A two-pass Codex app-server preflight discovers the generated session-hook hash, trusts only that unmanaged hook, disables all other unmanaged hooks, retains managed administrator hooks, and verifies the effective state before provider launch. The runtime does not use the global hook-trust bypass and writes no repository-local `.codex` or `.codex-conductor` state.
- Bound command-policy and hook identity through workflow fingerprints, resume, packet caches, traces, run metrics, dry-run/inspection output, and static/live dashboard detail. One preflight is reused across all packets in an `agent_map`; completed resume launches no new preflight or provider work.
- Added a restricted reviewer profile/workflow, public documentation, ten focused adversarial tests, and three parity smoke checks. The tests exercise parser bypass attempts, the actual embedded hook subprocess, external/managed hook state, CLI/schema lifecycle, single/fan-out execution, no-op resume, cache/trace/state evidence, and dashboard visibility. Also hardened app-server cleanup/early-exit handling, command-line hook-state size bounds, a rare first-writer agent-memory lock race, and standalone bundle coverage; the bundle now includes the safe saved workflow but excludes local Claude settings.
- The suite now has 569 passing tests and 46 passing parity smoke checks. Real no-provider Codex 0.143.0 probes verified strict argument parsing, stable hook trust, and suppression of a deliberately injected external hook. Three earlier bounded Codex model probes were attempted; only the allow-path probe reached and executed its permitted `pwd` call before its cap, while the deny probes reached no tool call. No Claude call was made; every future Claude lane remains forced to Sonnet plus Ultracode and rejects Opus.

## 0.40.0

- Added strict revisioned `conductor.agent_memory.v1` stores under external workspace state. Entries bind workspace/profile identity, content hashes and byte counts, tags, source provenance, monotonic revisions, secret-pattern redaction, global limits, mode-0600 atomic replacement, and per-profile advisory writer locking.
- Added profile `memory.mode: read-only|read-write` plus bounded snapshot limits. Every run receives an immutable newest-entry snapshot framed as untrusted and potentially stale context; revision/hash/count flow through workflow fingerprints, resume, checkpoints, packet caches, traces, state metrics, and dashboards.
- Added `remember-agent-memory`, `list-agent-memory`, `inspect-agent-memory`, `forget-agent-memory`, `validate-agent-memory`, and public `schema agent-memory`. Memory directories are rejected inside the workspace, inspection omits entry content, optimistic revision checks prevent lost updates, and idempotent entry IDs make interrupted writes safe to retry.
- Added approval-gated `agent_memory` workflow steps. Appends require a read-write profile, medium/high risk, `--allow-writes`, and `--approve agent-memory-write`; updates affect future runs only and one update per profile per workflow prevents ambiguous revision chains. Model-authored workflows cannot opt themselves into memory, and `run-goal` rejects pre-verification memory updates.
- Kept scheduled authorization stable by separating static profile/context binding from per-execution memory snapshots. New routine executions can consume the latest memory while an ordinary resumed run restores its original persisted snapshot.
- Added a profile-memory workflow, strict memory fixture, seven focused lifecycle/concurrency/security tests, and three parity smoke checks. The suite now has 559 tests and 43 smoke checks. No model or paid Claude call was made; every future Claude campaign lane remains Sonnet plus Ultracode and rejects Opus.

Changed files and verifier status are recomputed against staged evidence, shown by the CLI, and can satisfy deterministic final-reporting credit when a correct patch survives provider cutoff without prose; failed execution remains failed.
- Ran the first preregistered new-shape pair. Codex exhausted 20,000 weighted tokens but changed all three refactoring files, passed 4 visible plus 7 held-out tests, and scored 10/10. Claude was forced to Sonnet Ultracode, observed `claude-sonnet-5` with no Opus, spent `$0.1701073` against a `$0.15` request, changed two files, failed verification, and scored 0/10. Both terminal outcomes failed, and unlike cap enforcement keeps the comparison non-claim-eligible.
- Added campaign/schema/CLI/security-policy tests, end-to-end deterministic tests for all three new canaries, hidden mutation evaluation, safe added-file patch validation, and a 31-check parity smoke entry for campaign planning.

## 0.32.0

- Added opt-in ordered `command+model` verification to `run-goal`, `run-model-goal`, and `auto`. Supplying `--check-command-json` with `--check-prompt` or `--check-prompt-file` runs the deterministic command first and launches the read-only semantic verifier only after command success. Existing command-only and model-only behavior and fingerprints remain unchanged.
- Made the chain token-proportional and fail-closed. A failed or timed-out command records bounded feedback, marks the model stage skipped, and spends zero model-verifier calls. A passed command followed by an unsatisfied model verdict produces actionable retry feedback; model launch, telemetry, timeout, or malformed-verdict failures terminate as `verifier_failed`.
- Bound composite kind, order, component fingerprints, redacted metadata, short-circuit policy, and exact per-iteration model-verifier call count through goal resume, automatic-routing receipts, progressive escalation, and anonymous detached-worker payload validation. Legacy auto route versions cannot claim composite verification.
- Expanded static and live goal detail views to show command status, model status or skip, and model-verifier calls. Raw semantic criteria remain absent from goal, routing, background, and dashboard artifacts.
- Added end-to-end coverage for zero-call short-circuiting, successful command-then-model execution, fail-closed model errors, progressive direct-first escalation, verifier-fingerprint drift, automatic receipts, detached execution, and static/live UI evidence.

## 0.31.0

- Expanded the seeded implementation canary with `retry-policy-migration`, a two-file compatibility migration with four provider-visible tests, seven separately injected held-out tests, strict scope/signature checks, and deterministic scoring. The evaluator now selects fixtures by task id while preserving the original slug canary.
- Improved the Codex staged implementation prompt with a compact, task-independent cross-file contract review covering callers, signatures and input domains, error behavior, boundaries, compatibility conversions, and mutation. On one same-fixture exploratory rerun, held-out correctness improved from failing to 7/7 and the deterministic score rose from 5/10 to 9/10; the remaining point was lost because token exhaustion prevented the provider's final prose report.
- Made safely retained failed patches measurable. The canary evaluator accepts `verification-failed` staged evidence only when its validated patch stays within the expected implementation files, so unsuccessful executions receive evidence-backed scores instead of disappearing.
- Separated live provenance from task success. Claude and Codex manifests may now bind source-preserving, non-applied, verifier-unmutated `verification-failed` or `verification-timed-out` staged evidence with a retained patch. Drift, verifier mutation, unsafe metadata, patchless failures, and unsupported statuses remain ineligible.
- Ran a new matched migration trial. Claude was forced to Sonnet Ultracode, resolved `claude-sonnet-5` with a Haiku helper and no Opus, exceeded its `$0.10` request at `$0.1335503`, changed one of two files, and scored 1/10. The initial Codex run stopped at its 20,000-token cap, changed both files, passed visible tests, and scored 5/10. Different cap mechanisms, failed terminal outcomes, and one repetition make this exploratory evidence only.
- Added regression coverage for multi-file hidden evaluation, retained failed-patch scoring, safe terminal live manifests, unsafe verifier-mutation rejection, the staged contract-review prompt, and a 30-check packaged parity smoke that validates the expanded canary contract.

## 0.30.0

- Added `deterministic-v3` progressive automatic orchestration. With an explicit verifier and multi-worker envelope, `auto` now runs one bounded direct attempt first and spends on a model-authored graph only after verifier failure. `--strategy progressive` pins this policy; `--strategy direct` remains direct-only and `--strategy goal` still plans immediately.
- Preserved adaptive quality and resume semantics across escalation. The first direct attempt uses one worker and zero planner calls; the first failed verification feeds bounded untrusted evidence into a new planner session; later model-planned iterations resume that same session. Resume fingerprints and detached anonymous payloads bind progressive mode, and completed direct attempts are never replayed.
- Added per-iteration planning evidence plus goal/static/live aggregation of completed planner calls. Progressive views distinguish zero-call first-pass success from model escalation instead of inferring spend from session availability.
- Fixed risk-term classification so `auth` still matches scopes such as `auth/session.py`, `auth_service.py`, and `auth-token`, but no longer matches unrelated words such as `author`. This removes a false high-risk gate that could block every adaptive replan prompt while retaining authorization-sensitive escalation.
- Expanded auto receipt lifecycle statuses so legitimate blocked, paused, stopped, and terminated generated workflows remain valid evidence rather than causing receipt construction failure.
- Added direct-success, verified escalation, feedback propagation, no-replay resume, route-version tamper, planner-call accounting, detached-worker, risk-boundary, and blocked-workflow regression coverage.

## 0.29.0

- Added `deterministic-v2` direct automatic orchestration. The default serial `auto` route compiles one bounded Codex step without a planning call; an explicit verifier selects the corresponding direct adaptive goal with zero planner calls per iteration. `--strategy direct` pins that mode, while explicit multi-worker or `workflow`/`goal` strategies retain model-authored decomposition.
- Kept the direct path inside the existing security and evidence boundaries: complete dry-run preflight, `model-workflow-execute`, `model-workflow-write`, weighted rollout caps, strict workflow/planning/run/auto receipts, foreground or detached lifecycle, recovery checkpoints, redaction, and task-independent capability routing. Serial plan-only now launches zero provider processes.
- Added a dedicated direct prompt contract, explicit `ultra` effort support, model/effort provenance, direct-mode resume fingerprints and background payload validation, and static/live goal visibility that reports deterministic planning with zero planner calls instead of a missing planner session.
- Fixed adaptive auto background handoff status normalization so launch metadata `active`/`launching` records valid auto status `running` rather than failing receipt validation.
- Added adversarial provider-call-count, write-gate, adaptive, detached-worker, legacy receipt, schema, CLI, and dashboard coverage. A separately approved Claude audit used Sonnet Ultracode with no Opus, but exceeded its `$0.20` request at `$0.4349514` before producing findings; it remains failed safety evidence and was not retried.

## 0.28.0

- Added optional restart-persistent routine services for macOS launchd and Linux systemd user sessions. Installation, rotation, status, and removal are explicit CLI operations; Skill/runtime installation and transient supervision never enable a service.
- Added strict expiring `conductor.routine_service_grant.v1` authorization bound to exact packaged runtime bytes/path, explicit routine manifest bytes, target workflow fingerprints, capability coverage, platform, and bounded hash-only workflow approvals. Wildcard `all`, unlisted routines, raw persisted approvals, symlinked inputs, and drift fail closed.
- Added strict `conductor.routine_service_state.v1` heartbeat/counter evidence, duplicate-worker locking, restart-on-failure descriptors, manager-failure evidence, on-disk grant revalidation each cycle, and CLI/static/live visibility for descriptor, state, grant, heartbeat, PID, runtime, manifest, and target health.
- Added monthly `DAY:HH:MM` routine schedules with timezone validation, short-month final-day clamping, normal seven-day latest-slot catch-up, CLI create/update support, and public-schema coverage.
- Added public schemas, deterministic grant/state fixtures, 29 parity smoke checks, and adversarial launchd/systemd tests. The release does not enable a user service on installation and does not claim real login/reboot reliability until separately exercised.

## 0.27.0

- Added read-only `list-auto` and `status-auto` lifecycle views. They scan a bounded no-follow auto-receipt directory, validate every strict receipt, resolve only filename-plus-path-hash-bound child artifacts under expected external-state roots, and report handoff status separately from effective child status and liveness.
- Made detached auto workflows and adaptive goals first-class in static and live dashboards. Completed child receipts now resolve an immutable auto handoff from `running` to effective completion; missing, malformed, symlinked, stale, or path-drifted children surface as attention states rather than guessed success. Custom child locations require an explicitly supplied matching path.
- Kept claim semantics unchanged. Auto receipts describe routing/handoff, while existing child run and goal artifacts remain authoritative completion evidence in evidence bundles; the new visibility layer does not duplicate or promote routing metadata into parity evidence.
- Added redaction, directory/record bounds, malformed JSON, symlink, path-drift, workflow-background, goal-background, CLI, packaged-smoke, static dashboard, live payload, and HTML rendering coverage.

## 0.26.0

- Added `conductor-runtime auto`, a deterministic one-command front door over the existing model-workflow and adaptive-goal engines. No verifier selects one-shot workflow planning/execution; an explicit command or model verifier selects bounded adaptive replanning. Task text is never an authority for route or capability selection, and no extra routing-model call is spent.
- Added safe execution inference. Without `model-workflow-execute`, the one-shot route completes model planning and full dry-run preflight only. Adaptive and detached routes fail before provider launch without that approval. `--allow-writes` requests write-capable topology but execution still requires `model-workflow-write`; explicit parallel envelopes default to four workers and serial envelopes to one.
- Added strict `conductor.auto_orchestration_receipt.v1` evidence, a public JSON Schema, `validate-auto-receipt`, and an external-state default. Receipts store task hashes, deterministic route reasons, policy booleans, bounded limits, and hash-only artifact links without raw task or approval values. Detached receipts remain immutable handoff records and identify mutable child lifecycle evidence honestly.
- Updated the installed skill guidance to prefer `auto` for substantial Mode 3–5 runtime work while keeping Mode 0 and focused Mode 2 direct. Added foreground, adaptive, detached, privacy, tamper, pre-provider capability, CLI, schema, and smoke-fixture coverage.

## 0.25.0

- Added optional `agent_map.max_packets` batching to cap model-session count independently from source-item count. Source items remain individually validated, but a deterministic contiguous partition can encode multiple scopes as one JSON-array packet. Each packet is limited to 64 source items; an impossible ceiling fails before any provider process starts.
- Preserved recovery and cache correctness across grouped work. Packet identity binds the complete canonical item list, cache fingerprints bind every member's bounded file/directory content, any changed or uncacheable member invalidates the grouped result, and `retry-packet` reruns one grouped scope while retaining compatible sibling packets.
- Upgraded generated agent profiles to `balanced-v2`. Deterministic and model-authored planners plus bundled maps now use a 25-packet ceiling alongside the existing `medium`/4,000-per-call/100,000-per-attempt map budget. A synthetic runtime test proves that 1,000 source items become 25 calls of 40 scopes instead of 1,000 sessions, each retaining the intended 4,000-token cap.
- Added separate item/packet/call metrics to state and dashboard surfaces, including total/cached packets, source items per packet, configured packet ceiling, and existing budgeted invocation evidence. Existing workflows that omit `max_packets` preserve one-item-per-call behavior and legacy cache-detail wording.
- Added schema, validation, dynamic-source fail-before-launch, canonical packetization, reduced-call budget, content invalidation, targeted retry, dashboard, planner, and 1,000-item scheduler tests. This is deterministic efficiency control, not live evidence that grouped Codex review matches Claude quality or latency.

## 0.24.0

- Added optional bounded Codex effort and weighted rollout-token controls to ordinary workflows. Top-level `agent_effort`, `agent_max_tokens`, and `agent_map_max_total_tokens` provide defaults; `codex_exec.effort`/`max_tokens` and `agent_map.effort`/`max_tokens`/`max_total_tokens` provide step overrides. The runner passes these limits to the same runtime-hard experimental rollout-budget protocol used by the isolated Codex adapters, including resumed same-thread calls.
- Added fair `agent_map` budget allocation. A map's total budget is divided only across packets that still require provider work, cached packets consume no new allocation, and an underfunded map fails before any provider launch. Targeted retries and later workflow retries are explicit new execution attempts and therefore receive a newly bounded allocation.
- Made deterministic and model-authored planners plus the bundled agent workflows emit a balanced budget profile: `high` effort and 12,000 weighted rollout tokens for ordinary agents, 24,000 for write agents, and `medium` effort with 4,000 per packet plus 100,000 per map attempt. Existing hand-authored workflows remain compatible because all fields are optional. Dashboards expose configured effort, per-call limits, map-attempt limits, and budgeted invocation counts.
- Added schema, command-contract, resume, planner, dashboard, cache-aware allocation, high-scale compatibility, and fail-before-launch tests. The full suite now contains 488 passing tests.
- Ran a second live seeded implementation canary against one unchanged fixture. Claude was strictly pinned to Sonnet Ultracode, resolved to `claude-sonnet-5` with a Haiku helper and no Opus, stopped at its `$0.10` provider budget after `$0.1027594`, and took 25.251 seconds. Codex `gpt-5.6-sol` at `ultra` stopped at its 20,000 weighted rollout-token budget after 80.987 seconds. Both retained patches passed 3 visible and 5 held-out tests and scored 10/10, but both execution outcomes failed at their caps and the different cap units/enforcement keep the comparison non-claim-eligible. No broad parity or superiority claim follows.

## 0.23.0

- Added strict atomic `conductor.codex_step_checkpoint.v1` records for single `codex_exec` steps. The runtime consumes `thread.started` while the provider is still active, persists only bounded session/configuration hashes and safe metadata, and terminalizes the checkpoint with an output hash or failure class.
- Added explicit `recover-run --resume-codex` continuation. After proving the runner and tracked children inactive, recovery binds exactly one interrupted Codex step to the approved checkpoint bytes; the next normal `run --resume` starts a new turn on that same UUID-bound thread, requires matching resumed telemetry, and rejects workflow, prompt, model, sandbox, output, session, status, count, or post-approval checkpoint drift before provider launch.
- Kept uncertain outcomes explicit. Default recovery still marks interrupted work failed and `--retry-running` still starts fresh; same-thread continuation is never automatic, never replays the original prompt, and does not claim to resume the exact in-flight turn or recover uncertain token spend. Reset, retry, skip, and restart paths invalidate stale continuation bindings.
- Added hashed checkpoint visibility and same-thread guidance to diagnostics/static detail, a separate token-gated `Resume Codex thread` live action, CLI coverage, and interruption/tamper/stream-bound tests. Provider stdout is now consumed with availability-based reads so the checkpoint is durable before process completion, and invalid streamed events terminate the child promptly.

## 0.22.0

- Added execute-wide run ownership using a no-follow, single-link advisory lock. Concurrent `run --resume` attempts now fail before overwriting runner metadata, and direct retry/reset/skip/packet controls cannot race an active or interrupted runner.
- Added audited `recover-run` reconciliation for hard interruption windows. Recovery requires a free cross-process lock, local runner provenance, an inactive owner, and no live recorded child session; it can mark an uncertain running step failed, explicitly reset it for retry, or safely resume when interruption occurred between steps. Normal handled exceptions now finalize a running step as failed automatically instead of leaving false active state.
- Runner heartbeats now record bounded PID/process-group/session identities for active children without argv or command text. Diagnostics and the live UI expose guarded recovery, and recovered runner metadata is finalized with an audit record.
- Added atomic per-packet cache-entry receipts. Each completed `agent_map` packet persists its hash-bound cache evidence before returning, so recovery can reuse completed packets even if the aggregate cache manifest had not reached its next batch flush before process loss.

## 0.21.0

- Added audited `retry-packet RUN_DIR STEP_ID PACKET_INDEX` recovery for `agent_map` workflows. One selected failed or completed packet receives an item-hash-bound generation bump, its parent step becomes resumable, and compatible sibling packet outputs remain cache hits. Optional `--cascade` resets transitive downstream work without widening the selected upstream rerun.
- Added per-packet cache generations to run state and packet traces. Targeted retries bind the recorded packet index to its SHA-256 item identity, reject active runs, malformed traces/state, out-of-range or unobserved packets, and item-list drift before provider launch. Full step/reset/restart invalidation clears targeted bindings as the explicit recovery path after intentional item changes.
- Hardened all non-cached packet execution by removing a prior regular output before provider launch, preventing stale output from being mistaken for a new result after failure or no-output completion. Cache writes now prune superseded entries for the same packet output. Diagnostics, CLI output, run detail, static/live cache summaries, and token-gated live controls expose the packet-specific recovery path.

## 0.20.0

- Added atomic, hash-bound `conductor.codex_staged_repair_state.v1` checkpoints to bounded Codex repair. `--attempts-this-run` can stop cleanly after a chosen number of new attempts, and `--resume` revalidates the task, model/limits, verifier command hash, source, completed reports, and stage chain before continuing without replaying provider calls.
- Made interruption semantics explicit and fail closed. A checkpoint marked `attempt-active` is never replayed because the runtime cannot prove whether provider budget was consumed; completed attempts remain reusable, approval values and raw paths/commands are never persisted, active duration excludes downtime, and source/config/stage drift or checkpoint tampering blocks resume before launch.
- Added terminal-write recovery for an exact preexisting cumulative patch and for a repair receipt whose aggregate report was not yet written. Completed resumes are idempotent, while an orphan aggregate report is rejected. Added a read-only checkpoint validator, public JSON Schema, parity fixture, and a 25-check smoke suite.

## 0.19.0

- Added a truthful aggregate `benchmark-report.json` to every bounded Codex repair bundle. The report embeds and revalidates every hash-linked attempt report, carries the aggregate repair receipt, preserves unfavorable outcomes, and never represents only the final provider call as the whole run.
- Added `conductor.benchmark_quality_evidence.v2` for repair-backed scoring. It binds the task/output plus the complete repair receipt and embedded attempt-report sequence; strict v1 quality evidence remains supported for existing single-attempt reports.
- Integrated aggregate repair reports with live run manifests, comparison claim gates, safety-incident propagation, evidence collection, and dashboard summaries. Manifest token provenance now uses the authorized total repair cap, successful and exhausted deterministic trials remain distinguishable, and provider/invalid-stage failures remain ineligible for live binding.
- Added `validate-benchmark-report`, automatic one-level dashboard discovery for repair bundles, a packaged aggregate report fixture, and a 24-check parity smoke suite. Fixed a retry bug so a Codex token cutoff followed by verifier failure stops after one provider call instead of consuming another attempt.

## 0.18.0

- Added `run-codex-staged-repair`, a bounded source-isolated implementation loop that retries only deterministic `verification-failed` and `no-changes` outcomes. Each retry receives a fresh immutable copy of the preceding stage plus bounded redacted verifier diagnostics marked as untrusted; provider, source-drift, timeout, invalid-stage, metadata, and sandbox failures stop immediately.
- Added strict `conductor.codex_staged_repair.v1` evidence with preflighted worst-case token/time caps, aggregate rollout usage, a fingerprinted stage chain, hash-linked per-attempt benchmark reports, cumulative original-to-final change metadata, and a cumulative Git patch that is never auto-applied. Loading the receipt revalidates attempt reports and the final patch's byte count and SHA-256.
- Reduced avoidable staged-run latency by directing Codex to leave language-runtime and test execution to the deterministic post-turn verifier. Added adversarial tests for successful repair, retry exhaustion with retained cumulative work, provider-stop behavior, source immutability, approval secrecy, CLI overwrite protection, evidence/patch tampering, and command-risk classification.
- Added the `codex-staged-repair` public schema and a full non-live hash-linked fixture to the then-23-check parity smoke suite. Broad parity still requires repeated equivalent live trials and independent scoring.

## 0.17.0

- Upgraded current Codex provider evidence to `conductor.codex_provider_evidence.v3`. Runtime-budget accounting now matches the command-enforced Codex rollout formula: non-cached input plus output at 1.0 prefill/sampling weights. Gross terminal usage remains visible but no longer causes false cap failures when cache reuse keeps weighted usage within budget. Strict v1 and v2 validation/schema exports remain available.
- Preserved useful staged edits across clean provider budget cutoffs. Codex rollout exhaustion and Claude dollar-budget exhaustion still fail the provider outcome, but the adapters now run the deterministic verifier and retain a valid reviewable patch when the isolated source/stage contracts remain intact.
- Added a reproducible seeded implementation canary with provider-visible tests, held-out tests, and `tools/evaluate_implementation_canary.py`. The evaluator verifies the staged patch hash, applies it to a fresh workspace, runs exact visible and hidden test counts in the OS verifier sandbox, checks scope/signature/structure/reporting, and emits independently reproducible 10-point score input bound to all fixture and result hashes.
- Completed a matched live staged canary. Fresh Codex v3 evidence passed with 56,465 gross tokens, 39,936 cached input tokens, 16,529 rollout-budget tokens, zero overshoot, and 54.862 seconds. The paid comparison was forced to Sonnet Ultracode, observed `claude-sonnet-5` plus a Haiku helper and no Opus, cost `$0.0660063`, and finished in 27.817 seconds. Both patches passed 3 visible plus 5 held-out tests and scored 10/10. The structured comparison remains non-claim-eligible because provider-native dollar and weighted-token enforcement are not equivalent; this is one quality tie, not a broad parity or superiority claim.
- Updated dashboards to distinguish gross terminal tokens, rollout-budget tokens, rollout overshoot, and legacy gross-token overshoot. Added regression coverage for the exact cache-heavy live usage profile and retained compatibility for historical v1/v2 reports.

## 0.16.0

- Upgraded Codex provider evidence to `conductor.codex_provider_evidence.v2`. Codex runs now use explicit minimal permission profiles, sanitized model-shell environments, ignored project/user instructions, disabled network and optional tool surfaces, bounded tool output, and the experimental Codex rollout budget as a runtime-hard weighted token cap. Strict v1 validation remains available as `codex-provider-evidence-v1`.
- Added `run-codex-staged-task`, a source-isolated implementation adapter requiring agent, network, write, `codex-live-run`, and `codex-staged-write` gates. It grants Codex write access only to an external stage, runs a deterministic verifier under macOS Seatbelt or Linux bubblewrap, fingerprints the source throughout, and emits a reviewable Git patch without applying it.
- Added strict `conductor.codex_staged_evidence.v1`, CLI/schema/fixture validation, live-manifest binding, comparison cross-checks, runbook templates, security classification, and dashboard summaries for Codex staged runs. Source drift, invalid stages, binary or mode changes, verifier mutation/failure/timeout, provider cutoff, and patch races fail closed.
- Proved the current Codex CLI rollout-budget protocol with a bounded live probe: budget exhaustion emitted a terminal `turn.failed` event and stopped the turn. Added adversarial coverage for that terminal path, partial-output retention, v1 compatibility, staged source isolation, permission configuration, non-persisted approvals, and CLI overwrite safety. The feature remains explicitly labeled experimental in evidence.

## 0.15.0

- Added `run-codex-readonly-task`, a source-isolated Codex comparison adapter that requires an explicit model, reasoning effort, token cap, agent/network gates, and `codex-live-run` approval. It runs an ephemeral strict-config `codex exec` session in a read-only sandbox with user rules, plugins, browser tools, multi-agent features, and other optional capabilities disabled; fingerprints both source and external stage; and emits strict `conductor.codex_provider_evidence.v1` evidence.
- Added hash-bound benchmark scoring with strict score-input and `conductor.benchmark_quality_evidence.v1` artifacts. Scored reports preserve execution outcome separately from rubric outcome, bind the task contract, retained output, provider/staged evidence, reviewer identity, scale, and threshold, and require independent equivalent scoring before a comparison can become claim-eligible.
- Added explicit cost/token cap-enforcement provenance to run manifests and comparison equivalence. Clean provider budget cutoffs remain genuine live outcomes while malformed, rejected, timed-out, truncated, drifted, or otherwise invalid evidence still fails closed. Codex's current post-run token check and Claude's provider-side dollar cap can no longer be represented as equivalent enforcement.
- Completed one same-task, same-stage exploratory read-only pair. Codex `gpt-5.6-sol` at `ultra` produced a parent-scored 10/10 answer but used 326,572 tokens against a 100,000 post-run cap; Claude was explicitly pinned to Sonnet Ultracode, resolved to `claude-sonnet-5` with no Opus, cost `$0.0656049`, and received 2/10. Both final task outcomes failed for different reasons, and the comparison correctly remains non-claim-eligible because cap enforcement differed and the reviewer was not independent.

Source drift is checked after Claude and after verification; tracked verifier mutation, symlink/special-file injection, binary or mode changes, verifier failure, timeout, and output races fail closed.

## 0.12.0

- Added durable external routine controls with `pause-routine`, approval-gated `resume-routine`, `run-routine-now`, `status-routine`, and approval-gated atomic `update-routine-schedule` commands. The loopback live dashboard now exposes token-protected pause, resume, and run-now actions without embedding or persisting approval values.
- Added strict weekday and one-shot UTC schedules plus one-most-recent catch-up evaluation bounded to seven days. Paused, blocked, failed, interrupted, timed-out, and completed schedule outcomes now produce capped history while each due slot is consumed at most once.
- Added strict `conductor.routine_controls.v1` and `conductor.routine_supervisor.v1` control/history validation, public schemas, fixtures, CLI validators, duplicate-name preflight, list/static/live dashboard summaries, and active-worker tests proving schedule edits are observed without restart.
- Automatic run directories now use atomic collision suffixes so repeated or concurrent same-workflow launches within one second do not fail; explicit operator run IDs retain fail-if-exists behavior.
- Packaged runtime zipapps now include a portable Python shebang and executable mode, with an integration test that invokes the built artifact directly and checks archive integrity and bytecode exclusion.

## 0.11.0

- Added strict `conductor.background_routine_supervisor.v1` metadata and public JSON Schema, anonymous-pipe approval handoff, status/wait/validate/terminate commands, routine-list summaries, and static/live dashboard visibility without persisting approval values.
- Background routines now execute through the supervisor-owned `WorkflowRunner` instead of a nested CLI, preserving target fingerprints, policy gates, whole-routine time budgets, per-run evidence, and reliable cleanup of active step process groups. Blocked, failed, timed-out, interrupted, and successful executions remain visible in routine state and bounded logs.
- Added deterministic lifecycle fixtures and real subprocess integration tests for due execution, approval secrecy, duplicate prevention, blocked results, nonzero final status, active-child cleanup, and bounded or indefinite supervisor operation.

## 0.10.0

- Added same-session Codex planner continuity to adaptive model goals. The first iteration captures the canonical `thread.started` UUID and later iterations use `codex exec resume`, preserving the planner transcript while still authoring and validating a fresh complete workflow graph for every attempt.
- Bound resume to one strict UUID and resolved-workspace hash, rejected ambiguous, missing, or drifting resumed-session telemetry, reasserted read-only sandbox configuration on resumed calls, and added `--fresh-planner-session-per-iteration` as an explicit compatibility and isolation escape hatch.
- Persisted the resumable UUID only in external goal state, exposed only mode/availability/hash/turn evidence through list and dashboard APIs, threaded continuity through detached foreground-to-background resume, and added deterministic command-contract, identity-drift, privacy, integration, and packaged-fixture coverage.

## 0.9.0

- Added `run-model-goal --background`, which performs the same complete request, policy, verifier, limit, and resume-fingerprint validation before launching one session-isolated adaptive model-goal worker with no daemon installation or restart policy.
- Added strict `conductor.background_model_goal.v1` lifecycle metadata, worker readiness/heartbeat evidence, anonymous-pipe task and approval handoff, and `validate-`, `status-`, `wait-`, and `terminate-background-model-goal` commands.
- Added graceful-first force escalation, active planner process-group cleanup, interrupted goal finalization, CLI/list/static/live dashboard visibility, public JSON Schema export, parity fixture validation, and real detached-worker integration tests for success, preflight rejection, secrecy, and termination.

## 0.8.0

- Added `run-model-workflow --background`, a one-command read-only model planning, complete policy preflight, and explicit detached execution path using the isolated per-run worker introduced in 0.7.0.
- Versioned model workflow run receipts as `conductor.model_workflow_run_receipt.v3`: detached receipts begin in `running`, are hash-bound at launch, and are atomically finalized by the worker without persisting the receipt path or approval values in background metadata. Strict v1 and v2 validation/schema exports remain available.
- Added fail-closed receipt tamper detection, prepared-policy drift rejection, foreground/dry-run compatibility tests, CLI integration coverage, and foreground plus detached receipt templates in the parity smoke suite.

## 0.7.0

- Added explicit detached workflow runs with `start-background-run`, `status-background-run`, and `wait-background-run`, backed by the same complete prepared-run policy preflight as foreground execution.
- Added strict `conductor.background_run.v1` metadata and public JSON Schema, external-state dashboard/list visibility, per-run worker logs, session isolation, no-restart semantics, and one-time approval handoff over an anonymous pipe without persisting approval values.
- Extended validated `terminate-run` control so graceful detached-worker termination also kills and reaps active step process groups, with integration coverage for launch, approval secrecy, status, wait, preflight failure, dashboard visibility, tamper rejection, and child cleanup.

## 0.6.1

- Made model workflow planning explicitly default to `high` reasoning effort instead of inheriting a potentially expensive user-level `xhigh` setting; added `--planner-effort` to plan, run, and adaptive-goal commands, with `xhigh` remaining opt-in.
- Recorded planner effort and planning timeout/output limits in strict planning and run receipts and bound adaptive-goal resume fingerprints to the selected effort.
- Made `run-model-workflow` fail closed with a validated failed-attempt run receipt when planning times out or otherwise fails, without creating a workflow run or attempting preflight/execution.
- Versioned the expanded planning and run receipts as `v2` while retaining validation and public schema exports for strict legacy `v1` receipts.

## 0.6.0

- Added `run-model-workflow`, an explicitly approved foreground task-to-plan-to-preflight-to-execution path that reuses the audited runner and starts no workflow process before a complete dry-run policy preflight succeeds.
- Added validated `conductor.model_workflow_run_receipt.v1` handoff receipts, a public JSON Schema, strict receipt validation, task/workflow/planning hashes, policy summaries without approval values, and completed/blocked/dry-run execution evidence.
- Added `run-model-goal`, which creates a fresh validated model-authored workflow on each bounded foreground iteration, feeds redacted verifier feedback into the next planning task as untrusted evidence, supports command or fail-closed model verification, and resumes only with matching task/planner/verifier fingerprints.
- Added dedicated `model-workflow-execute` approval, retained fixed `model-workflow-write` gate ancestry, and fail-fast checks for missing agent, write, parallel, and high-scale capabilities before a planning model is called.

## 0.5.0

- Added `plan-model-workflow`, an explicit read-only Codex workflow architect that writes a strict validated declarative draft and never executes it automatically.
- Updated live parity runbooks to compare approval-required model-authored Conductor planning against Claude/Ultracode while retaining a separate deterministic planning baseline and receipt artifacts.
- Classified validated live parity runbooks, run manifests, and evidence bundles as planned/provenance/index artifacts instead of surfacing them as unknown report warnings.
- Added model-draft policy validation for supported fields, bounded graph/worker/item limits, read-only workspace-scoped shell commands, read-only parallel agents, task-derived risk escalation, and fixed manual-gate ancestry for optional write-capable Codex steps.
- Added validated `conductor.model_workflow_receipt.v1` provenance receipts with task hashes instead of raw task text, normalized provider usage, review-required/no-process-started evidence, external default storage, schema export, and receipt validation CLI support.

## 0.4.0

- Added fail-closed read-only Codex goal verification with strict structured verdicts, prompt hashing instead of prompt persistence, automatic provider telemetry, and bounded redacted dashboard evidence.
- Made goal iterations adaptive by feeding bounded redacted command/model verifier feedback into the next workflow's Codex prompts as explicitly untrusted evidence.
- Raised the hard `agent_map` worker ceiling to 128 while preserving the 16-worker default safety boundary: actual concurrency above 16 requires `--approve high-scale-agent-map` in addition to agent and parallel capabilities, and a synthetic 128-packet test exercises the scheduler without paid provider calls.

## 0.3.0

- Moved all default runtime state to workspace-scoped directories under `~/.codex/conductor` (or `CODEX_CONDUCTOR_HOME`) and removed repo-local runtime artifacts and examples.
- Added automatic structured Codex CLI event and measured token capture for `codex_exec` and `agent_map` steps.
- Added explicitly approved routine execution plus an operator-visible foreground scheduler with interval/daily/weekly due checks, target fingerprint validation, timeouts, external state, and bounded logs.
- Added gated Codex Cloud submit/status/review/apply commands; apply requires a matching review receipt and verifies the cloud diff hash before mutation.
- Added dependency-free `conductor-runtime.pyz` and combined release-bundle packaging.
- Added proportionality guidance so focused work avoids unnecessary artifacts, delegation, and token overhead.

## 0.2.0

- Added `conductor_runtime/`, an optional standard-library Python runtime outside the installable prompt-only skill folder.
- Added declarative JSON workflows under `conductor-workflows/` for repo audits, bugfix reproduction, parallel review, implementation packets, and verification sweeps.
- Added runtime support for visible run artifacts, resumable `state.json`, dry-run planning, manual approval gates, redacted shell logs, Codex `exec` steps, and bounded `agent_map` fan-out.
- Added `docs/runtime.md` and README runtime usage notes.
- Added focused runtime unit tests while preserving the text-only `codex-conductor/` skill contract.
- Hardened runtime execution after multi-agent review: bounded subprocess output capture, timeout failure state, workspace-relative path checks, dependency validation, resume workflow fingerprints, manual-gate rechecks on resume, redacted workflow manifests, stricter command policy classification, and dry-run agent policy enforcement.
- Added dynamic `agent_map` item expansion from `items`, `items_file`, or `items_artifact`, plus `dynamic-runtime-review.json` and gated `bulk-row-review.json` workflow templates.
- Added `conductor_runtime benchmark`, `benchmark-suites/conductor-smoke.json`, and `docs/benchmarks.md` for repeatable local benchmark reporting.
- Added a sourced Claude Code/Ultracode capability inventory, parity task fixtures, comparison manifest template, and `conductor_runtime compare` for machine-readable benchmark report comparisons.
- Hardened benchmark/comparison handling: validated suite defaults and output limits, validated parity budgets, rejected unsafe comparison report paths, validated benchmark report shape, rejected duplicate task IDs, recomputed summaries from task results, and gated external tool version probes behind explicit approval.
- Hardened shell command classification so shell wrappers, Git shell aliases, and opaque inline interpreter code are destructive-gated; updated verification sweep metadata so local unittest discovery no longer requires network permission.
- Added benchmark run manifests plus `validate-run-manifest`; comparison reports can now include model/budget/permission provenance, score summaries, and safety incident summaries when per-system manifests are supplied.
- Added `conductor_runtime dashboard`, a static HTML run browser for workflow state, standard artifacts, benchmark reports, and comparison provenance with escaped, redacted, bounded artifact excerpts.
- Added run recovery controls: `retry-step`, `reset-step`, and `skip-step` with downstream cascade support, redacted audit events, symlink checks, and resume behavior for explicitly skipped dependencies.
- Added `conductor_runtime plan-workflow`, a deterministic workflow draft generator for task text, task files, failing commands, verification commands, gated write-capable implementation steps, and validated generated workflow JSON.
- Hardened workflow draft/runtime gates after review: generated no-agent workflows now preserve reproduction dependencies for cascade recovery, task prompt markers are escaped, secret-like generated workflow names and command inputs are rejected, task-file/output symlink ancestry is checked, external path shell arguments require explicit approval, more `find`/`git` destructive forms are gated, and workflow timeouts are schema-bounded.
- Added packetized `plan-workflow` generation: explicit packet items, workspace item files, and workspace globs can now produce bounded read-only `agent_map` review steps with validation and graph dependencies.
- Hardened packet sources after review: inline, glob, workspace-file, and artifact-file items now share validation for path scope, size/count bounds, secret-like values, prompt-boundary markers, symlink ancestry, high-risk scope escalation, and allowed `prompt_template` format fields.
- Added local per-item `agent_map` cache reuse for compatible retry/resume runs, with workflow/reset-generation/item/prompt/sandbox/model/workspace-file/output hashing, reset-step invalidation, redacted agent logs, atomic cache writes, and symlink-aware cache/output validation.
- Added `conductor_runtime serve`, a standard-library loopback-default live dashboard with auto-refreshing run and benchmark summaries plus out-of-band token-gated retry/reset/skip controls that reuse the audited run-control path.
- Added deterministic runtime metrics for new runs: run/step timestamps and durations, step kind/attempt metadata, process output metrics, and `agent_map` item/cache/worker counts surfaced in dashboard and live views while leaving token/cost totals unavailable unless real usage data is recorded.
- Added bounded run detail drill-downs to the static and live dashboards, including step metadata, standard artifact excerpts, artifact/log listings, redaction, HTML escaping, symlink skipping, and path-safe selected-run resolution.
- Added policy-gated local workflow hooks for `before_run`, `after_run`, `before_step`, and `after_step` quality gates, with fail-open/fail-closed modes, redacted logs, state evidence, dry-run planning, resume-safe execution, and dashboard visibility.
- Hardened hook and shell policy review findings: pathful executables are not trusted by basename, broad nested `python -m conductor_runtime` execution is no longer treated as read-only, `awk`/`sed` are gated as scriptable tools, hook exceptions record failure state, dry-run resumes skip already planned steps, legacy redacted workflow manifests resume correctly, final hooks keep runs non-terminal while executing, and agent output artifacts are bounded.
- Added audited step-boundary run controls: `pause-run`, `resume-run`, and `stop-run` in the CLI plus token-gated live dashboard forms. These record redacted, length-capped control events, use a shared run-control lock, are honored before the next workflow step starts, and do not kill an already-running subprocess.
- Added `restart-run` and `save-run-workflow`: restart resets all workflow steps without deleting artifacts/logs, invalidates `agent_map` cache generations, and is available from CLI plus token-gated live controls; workflow export writes a validated, redacted JSON copy to a new non-symlink destination for reuse.
- Added optional workflow step `phase` metadata and phase summaries in static/live dashboards plus `/api/state`, including phase status, step counts, local elapsed duration, agent invocation/item/cache counts, and recorded token/cost totals when present.
- Added safe saved workflow commands under `.claude/workflows/*.js`/`.mjs`: `validate-saved-workflows`, `list-saved-workflows`, `inspect-saved-workflow`, `export-saved-workflow`, and `run-saved-workflow` parse JSON-compatible `meta` and `workflow` exports without evaluating JavaScript, then reuse the audited workflow runner and policy gates.
- Expanded saved workflow commands with nested project discovery, optional personal workflow discovery, deterministic nearest-project/project-over-personal precedence, and bounded `--arg KEY=VALUE` placeholder rendering that revalidates the workflow before inspect/export/run.
- Added `plan-workflow --saved-command`, which writes a generated workflow draft directly as a safe `.claude/workflows/*.js`/`.mjs` saved command with JSON-compatible exports, no JavaScript execution, existing-destination and symlink rejection, and the same saved-workflow validation path used by runtime commands.
- Added `write-run-manifest`, which generates a validated run manifest from a benchmark report with explicit repository/model/budget/permission provenance and default pass/fail scoring for local live evidence.
- Added `compare --require-claim-eligible`, an opt-in fail-closed gate for scripts that should only proceed when all compared systems have equivalent live run provenance.
- Added `record-usage`, which records operator-supplied measured token/cost usage for a run or step, audits the update, and exposes totals through existing dashboard usage fields.
- Added `import-usage`, which imports measured usage from bounded local JSON artifacts and records it through the same audited usage path without provider or billing API calls.
- Added per-run `runner.json` heartbeat and owner metadata for active/final workflow visibility, surfaced in static and live dashboards without adding a hidden daemon or OS process manager.
- Added runner liveness classification for heartbeat metadata: dashboard/live summaries and `status --with-runner` now distinguish recently alive active runners from stale active runner metadata while preserving default raw `status` output.
- Added `list-runs`, a read-only CLI snapshot of recent runs with status, workflow, progress counts, runner liveness, status filtering, and compact redacted JSON output for automation.
- Hardened saved workflow reads and exports with component-wise no-follow parent directory opens and export-parent creation to close intermediate-ancestor symlink races.
- Hardened `save-run-workflow` exports with shared component-wise no-follow destination parent creation, final `dir_fd` file creation, and no-follow source `workflow.json` reads.
- Hardened run artifact IO with fd-relative no-follow helpers for run creation, resume path checks, state and standard artifact replacement, artifact/log reads and writes, packet item files, and agent-map cache/output hashing and redaction.
- Added live selected-run workflow JSON export at `/run/<handle>/workflow.json`, with validated redacted JSON, private metadata stripping, attachment headers, and no server-side destination write.
- Added dedicated `agent_map` packet detail tables to static and live run detail views, including bounded item labels, cache evidence, output/stdout/stderr excerpts, redaction, escaping, and symlink-safe cache handling.
- Added redacted local `agent_map` packet trace rows for executed, failed, output-missing, timed-out, and cached-reuse items; static and live packet detail tables now show trace status, timing, cache reuse, return code, timeout flag, and stdout/stderr byte counts when available.
- Raised local `agent_map` scale boundaries to align with the documented Ultracode comparison target: workflow validation and `plan-workflow` allow up to 16 workers, planner-generated packet sources allow up to 1,000 items, and parallel execution still requires explicit agent and parallel capability flags.

## 0.1.3

- Fixed a regression in `tools/grep_dangerous_terms.py`'s 0.1.2 `rm` detector: it only matched `rm` at the very start of a command segment, so any prose before it (a bullet, "Never do:", a numbered step, "Then run...") made a dangerous `rm -rf` invisible to the scanner. Now matches `rm` as a whole word anywhere in its command segment (still segment-scoped, so an unrelated command sharing the line can't supply the flags). Documented a known, accepted limitation: flags supplied indirectly via a separate process's output (e.g. `echo -r | xargs rm -f`) aren't detectable by a static line scanner.
- Fixed `tools/run_local_audit.py`'s new dangling-reference check to strip fenced code blocks before scanning, so an illustrative example path inside a ` ``` ` block in SKILL.md no longer fails the audit.
- Corrected PROJECT_SPEC.md's Amendments disclaimer, which cited the wrong section numbers (14.6/14.7, which have no such content) for the still-stale `Output sections` template text (actually in sections 15.1/15.3).
- Updated `tests/expected-behavior.md` to use "Codex Cloud task workflow" instead of the retired "Cloud handoff" naming for Mode 6, matching SKILL.md and `references/mode-selection.md`.
- Reworded `codex-conductor/SKILL.md` Workflow step 4, which had become a vacuous "if non-trivial" check once the Mode-0 fast path already filters out trivial tasks; now keyed to the risk level of the mode selected in step 2.
- Added a `## Risks / caveats` field to the Plan / Approval Response template in `references/response-templates.md` (previously the only response template with no field for disclosing a suspected prompt injection, despite being the template used for high-risk/unapproved work).
- `codex-conductor/SKILL.md`'s Mode-0 fast path and `references/delegation-contract.md` now both make explicit that a detected instruction-override must still be disclosed in the final answer, even when the rest of the workflow or artifact chain is skipped.

## 0.1.2

- Resolved the implicit-invocation self-contradiction between PROJECT_SPEC.md section 8 and the shipped `agents/openai.yaml`; documented the decision in a new PROJECT_SPEC.md "Amendments" section.
- Tightened SKILL.md's frontmatter description with concrete scope and exclusions instead of unbounded "auto-trigger whenever it might materially help" wording.
- Added a Mode 0 fast path for trivial requests (typo/one-line fixes) with no classification ceremony.
- Renamed Mode 6 from "cloud handoff" to "Codex Cloud task workflow" and pointed it at the real `codex cloud exec`/`codex apply` mechanism (the name "handoff" refers to a different, unrelated Codex feature).
- Added a risk-tier precedence rule to `references/mode-selection.md` for tasks matching multiple tiers.
- Broadened `references/security-gates.md`'s untrusted-input guidance to cover descriptive/contextual claims and impersonated system/developer formatting, and added a concrete Suspected Prompt Injection procedure with a defined report location.
- Reconciled `references/delegation-contract.md`'s canonical Agent Result schema with the bespoke output-section lists in `codex-agents/*.toml`; added a "suspicious or injected content observed" field and a secret-handling instruction requirement for subagent prompts; named Codex's built-in `default`/`worker`/`explorer` subagent roles as the no-custom-agent fallback.
- Fixed `agents/openai.yaml`'s invalid `icon` field (the documented schema uses `icon_small`/`icon_large`; removed since this skill ships no image assets).
- Fixed `tools/run_local_audit.py`'s `check_openai_policy()` to parse YAML correctly (comment- and formatting-aware) instead of a raw substring match, honoring `allow_implicit_invocation` only as a direct child of the `policy:` block (not a same-named key nested deeper under an unrelated sub-mapping); added a reciprocal check in `check_scenarios()` for undeclared scenario files; and added a new dangling-reference check in `check_references_linked()` that fails if `SKILL.md` mentions a `references/*.md` file that doesn't exist on disk.
- Fixed `tools/detect_unicode_controls.py` to also catch invisible/steganographic-injection code points (variation selectors, the Tags block) outside the Cf/Cc categories.
- Fixed `tools/grep_dangerous_terms.py` to catch realistic curl/wget-pipe-to-shell and `rm` recursive-force variants instead of one narrow literal spelling.
- Fixed `tools/package_skill.py` to always write root-relative zip arcnames, preventing a corrupt/non-portable package when invoked with an absolute path.
- Added a missing-directory guard to `audit_text_only.py`, `detect_unicode_controls.py`, and `grep_dangerous_terms.py` so a typo'd path fails loudly instead of silently reporting `OK`.
- Removed the hardcoded personal absolute path from README.md's Validate section; added a caveat about Codex skill-discovery path drift across versions and named the built-in subagent roles in the Optional Agents section.
- Collapsed `codex_conductor_project_spec.md` into a pointer to the now-canonical `PROJECT_SPEC.md`, removing a byte-identical duplicate with no source of truth.
